# Luciel — Drifts (Open and Resolved)

**What this document is:** The single ledger of every gap between the design (`ARCHITECTURE.md` + `CANONICAL_RECAP.md`) and the implementation (this repository, and the running production environment in AWS `ca-central-1`). Each gap is a token with a stable id, a status, and a resolution path.

**What this document is not:** A changelog. A version-history dump. A historical narrative. Closed drifts stay in the doc with a strikethrough so the audit chain of decisions remains walkable, but the document does not accumulate sediment beyond that.

**Maintenance protocol:** Surgical edits only. New drifts are appended with a unique id. Closed drifts get the closing commit/tag noted and the heading wrapped in strikethrough (`~~`). Reopened drifts get a new id; the original stays closed.

---

## Section 1 — Status legend and id scheme

**Status values:**

- `OPEN` — gap exists; no fix in flight
- `IN-PROGRESS` — fix is in flight on a named branch or PR
- `RESOLVED` — fix has landed on `main`; closing commit/tag noted; heading wrapped in `~~strikethrough~~`
- `DEFERRED` — gap acknowledged, deliberate decision to not fix this cycle; rationale recorded inline
- `WONTFIX` — gap re-examined and judged not a drift (design changed, or claim was wrong); rationale recorded inline

**Implementation marker scheme** (used in `ARCHITECTURE.md` and `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` once Phase 2 reconciliation begins applying them):

- ✅ Implemented — repo and prod both match the design
- 🔧 Partial — repo or prod implements some of the design; gaps tracked as drifts here
- 📋 Planned — design committed, no implementation yet; tracked as drift here
- 🔬 Decision-gate — design says "we will choose later"; not a drift, an open product decision

**Drift id scheme:** `D-<short-slug>-YYYY-MM-DD`. The date is when the drift was first opened, not when it was discovered later. Slug is short, hyphenated, and stable — never rename a slug after creation.

**Source of truth:** When this document, the architecture document, the canonical recap, the repository, or production disagree, the resolution is recorded here as a drift. The four artifacts converge by closing drifts, not by editing one and hoping the others catch up.

---

## Section 2 — Phase 2A repo reconciliation: how this register was built

This document was rebuilt on 2026-05-09 by walking `ARCHITECTURE.md` and `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` section by section against the repository at commit `c3ed8b6` on `main`. The previous DRIFTS.md (a partial, history-shaped register) was archived to `docs/archive/DRIFTS_pre-reconciliation.md` rather than discarded; that file remains the historical record up to that point.

The comparison covered:

- Architecture §2 — Development environment
- Architecture §3 — Production environment (every subsection)
- Architecture §4 — Cross-cutting properties
- Architecture §5 — Conceptual model
- Canonical Recap §1 — The two layers (Soul and Profession)
- Canonical Recap §2 — Six components
- Canonical Recap §3 — Cognitive abilities
- Canonical Recap §4 — Behavior contracts
- Canonical Recap §6 — Operating loop
- Canonical Recap §10 — Fixed-vs-configurable matrix
- Canonical Recap §11 — Eight strategic answers
- Canonical Recap §13 — End-to-end testing scenarios

Every drift below is tagged with the section that raised it. Production-only drifts (where the repo matches the design but production does not, or where we cannot tell from the repo alone) are tagged `[PROD-PHASE-2B]` and will be confirmed during Phase 2B with the operator at the PowerShell.

## Section 3 — Open drifts (repository scope)

### D-pilot-live-evidence-step-21-redo-and-step-23-deferred-2026-05-16
**Status:** OPEN — deferred-verification carve-out. The closing tag `step-30a-2-pilot-complete` is being cut today (2026-05-16) on this doc-truthing commit under an explicit user direction ("Doc-truth + cut closing tag now anyway", 2026-05-16 09:41 EDT), even though two of the original Step 30a.2-pilot GATE 4 live-smoke verification legs have not yet returned a green run: (a) **Step 2.1 redo** — a fresh $100 CAD live purchase against the Commit 3j (`43b2614`) image (`luciel-backend:59`, `step30a2-pilot-43b2614-r1`) that proves both the post-refund SES courtesy-email V3 leg (buyer inbox actually receives the "Your VantageMind pilot has been refunded" mail) and the V4 leg (CloudWatch log marker `[pilot-refund-email]` fires the SES-success line, not the SES-failure line); (b) **Step 2.3** — a repeat-customer attempt against an email Stripe already knows about, proving the upstream `BillingService.is_first_time_customer` gate short-circuits with a 403 + `error.code='not_first_time_customer'` and that the repeat customer cannot be billed the intro fee a second time. The Commit 3j code path is contract-test-proven (12/12 facets in `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3j.py`, 84/84 full Step 30a.2-pilot regression) and the underlying SES transport is prod-proven on the magic-link mint path that landed earlier in this arc — but neither leg has been observed firing on the live wire under the specific Step 30a.2-pilot `/pilot-refund` post-commit hook, and the repeat-customer 403 has never been observed on a live Stripe customer.
**Section that raised it:** GATE 5 doc-truthing pass on Step 30a.2-pilot close, 2026-05-16. Raised as the explicit integrity-view counterpart to the closing-tag decision so the gap is recorded honestly rather than hidden inside a confident-sounding recap row.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16 09:43 EDT during GATE 5 doc-truthing. The partner's framing ("the three canonical docs triangulate the business as three independent substantive views … the integrity view (DRIFTS) honestly records every time we fell short") makes this drift load-bearing on the doctrine itself: closing the tag without this drift would constitute a doctrine breach.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2-pilot row commits the success criterion that a real human can sign up, pay, use the product for 90 days, refund themselves, AND receive a courtesy email at the buyer-email address — with the five-leg verification (Stripe Dashboard refund + cancel; DB audit chain row_hash continuity; customer inbox; CloudWatch log marker; subscription + tenant row state) green per pilot purchase. The first full $100 CAD purchase→refund cycle (Stripe refund `pyr_1TXXwHRytQVRVXw7BGiHdxiJ`, 2026-05-15 to 2026-05-16) hit four of five legs cleanly (V1 Stripe Dashboard, V2 DB audit chain rows 4234–4238, V5 subscription + tenant row state, plus the on-page refund-success surface), but the V3 inbox leg and V4 CloudWatch leg were known to be unsupported on the Commit 3i image (no email handler at all) and the post-Commit-3j cycle that would carry both has not yet been run end-to-end. The repeat-customer 403 (Step 2.3) was never reached in the original sequence because Step 2.2 attempt 3 closed the refund and the user pivoted to GATE 5 doc-truthing before Step 2.3 was attempted.
**Repo state:** All Commit 3j code is on `main` at `43b2614`, live at task-def `luciel-backend:59`, image `step30a2-pilot-43b2614-r1`. `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3j.py` passes 12/12; full Step 30a.2-pilot regression passes 84/84. The Step 2.1 redo runbook (`/home/user/workspace/step_2_1_redo_runbook.md` on the advisor side) was authored and Block 1 (fresh Stripe Checkout under `aryans.www+pilot-smoke-20260516a@gmail.com`) executed against the `:59` image; Block 1 completed the live Stripe charge but the buyer landed on `/account/billing` rendering "NO SUBSCRIPTION ON FILE" — a separate observed surface tracked at `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16` below. The advisor attempted to diagnose via `aws ecs execute-command` with a multi-line `python -c` payload reading from the prod DB; the diagnostic was blocked by PowerShell argument splitting on the user's local shell (tracked at `D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16` below). The combination of the unresolved /account/billing surface bug and the diagnostic friction caused the partner to pivot to GATE 5 doc-truthing rather than push through.
**Operational impact today:** Low-to-medium. The Commit 3j email handler is contract-test-proven and the SES transport is prod-proven on a sibling path, so the probability that the courtesy email actually fails to deliver on the next live cycle is small — but probability is not proof. The closing tag carries the same caveat as Step 30a's original 2026-05-13 closure ("code-complete" naming code + contract tests + image, not prod-runtime live evidence). A real customer hitting the refund button on Commit 3j today would receive their money back, their subscription canceled, and their tenant deactivated — the financial cascade is on the four V1/V2/V5 legs that ARE proven — but the courtesy-email V3 leg might silently log an audit row with `action='pilot_refund_email_send_failed'` instead of delivering the mail, and the operator would only discover that on the next CloudWatch grep of `[pilot-refund-email]`. The repeat-customer 403 is even lower-impact: the upstream gate is contract-test-proven on the same paid-intro code path that the first live purchase exercised cleanly, so the probability of regression is small.
**Owning roadmap step:** Next billing-touch step. Likely Step 30b (widget chat first paying customer arc — which exercises the post-Step-30a billing surface as a side-effect once REMAX Crossroads completes a real signup) or a dedicated Step 30a.2-pilot-followup if one is scheduled before then. The exact owner will be assigned the next time a billing-surface change is in flight; this drift carries the gap until then.
**Resolution path:** A 30-minute live-smoke session at the next billing-touch window. (a) Fresh Stripe Checkout under a new `aryans.www+pilot-smoke-<date>@gmail.com` against the running `:59` (or successor) image; (b) verify the buyer receives the magic-link email and lands on `/account/billing` with the pilot ribbon and refund CTA visible (which also closes `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16` if the surface bug was a webhook race rather than a real implementation gap); (c) click `Refund my $100 intro fee`; (d) verify all five legs green: Stripe Dashboard shows Refunded + Cancelled, DB audit chain extends with the next five rows (refund, cancel, audit row, cascade, post-commit email row) with `row_hash` continuity, the buyer inbox receives the "Your VantageMind pilot has been refunded" mail, CloudWatch `/ecs/luciel-backend` shows `[pilot-refund-email]` SES-success line, subscription row is `canceled` and tenant_config is deactivated; (e) immediately initiate a second Stripe Checkout under the same buyer email (now flagged in our customers table) and verify the 403 + `error.code='not_first_time_customer'` short-circuit before any Stripe-side charge fires. The closure evidence is the five-leg green table for the new pilot cycle plus the 403 evidence for the repeat-customer attempt, appended to the original 2026-05-15 first-cycle evidence in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2-pilot row.
**Pattern E:** Pure verification — no code change, no schema change, no SDK pin change, no contract change. The drift closes by observation, not by mutation.
**Validation evidence:** None yet on the wire post-Commit-3j. First-cycle evidence (the four-of-five legs green) is recorded in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2-pilot row and at `~~D-pilot-refund-endpoint-and-website-surface-2026-05-15~~` above. Closure of this drift will append the second-cycle V3 + V4 evidence plus the Step 2.3 repeat-customer 403 evidence.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2-pilot row (the row whose closing-tag commit this drift is the integrity-view counterpart to); CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶273 (Intro refund policy — the customer-communication leg this drift's V3 verification proves on the wire); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the five atomic side effects of `BillingService.process_pilot_refund` — the fifth side effect is the post-commit SES email this drift's V3 leg verifies); `~~D-pilot-refund-customer-email-missing-2026-05-15~~` (the predecessor drift Commit 3j closed in code; this drift carries the deferred live-wire verification of that closure); `~~D-pilot-refund-endpoint-and-website-surface-2026-05-15~~` (the parent drift of the Commit 3a–3j arc — closed by the same arc, with this drift carving out the verification gap); `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16` (the observed surface bug that blocked Step 2.1 redo Block 2 — may be a precondition to closing this drift's V3 leg, or may be independent); `D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16` (the diagnostic friction that contributed to the pivot to GATE 5 rather than push through Step 2.1 redo Block 2).

### D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16
**Status:** OPEN — observed live surface bug, root cause not yet diagnosed. Step 2.1 redo Block 1 (2026-05-16 ≈09:30 EDT) completed a fresh Stripe Checkout against `luciel-backend:59` (Commit 3j image `step30a2-pilot-43b2614-r1`) under buyer email `aryans.www+pilot-smoke-20260516a@gmail.com`. The Stripe Checkout success_url redirected the buyer to `/account/billing` on the marketing site, which rendered the surface "NO SUBSCRIPTION ON FILE / You're signed in, but we don't see a paid subscription for this account." The buyer was therefore signed in (the session cookie minted), but the marketing site's `/me` query returned a shape that the Account page rendered as no-subscription. The buyer also reported "I subscribed but I have gotten any magic link in my email", which suggests the upstream magic-link mint may also have not fired — either the cookie was set by a different mechanism, or the magic-link was delivered to a different inbox-side filter.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.2-pilot Step 2.1 redo Block 1 verification, 2026-05-16. The surface was screen-captured by the buyer and shared with the advisor (`image.jpg`, the "NO SUBSCRIPTION ON FILE" pane on `/account/billing`).
**Raised by:** Aryan (operator) on 2026-05-16 ≈09:35 EDT, by sharing the screen capture mid-Step-2.1-redo. Computer (advisor) attempted a DB-side diagnostic (`aws ecs execute-command` with `python -c` reading from the prod DB for the user row, subscription row, audit-log tail, and webhook-event reception state) but was blocked by the sibling drift `D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16` and the diagnostic was abandoned.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row ("a new individual customer can find Luciel on our website, sign up, pay through Stripe Checkout, land on a magic-link confirm page, and reach a working dashboard") and CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2-pilot row ("a real human can land on `https://www.vantagemind.ai/pricing`, click Start 90-day pilot, complete Stripe Checkout for $100 CAD against a live card, receive a magic-link email through SES, land on `/account/billing` cookied, click Refund my $100 intro fee") jointly require that a successful Stripe Checkout under a fresh email produces (a) a magic-link email at the buyer-email address, (b) a session cookie when the buyer clicks the magic link, and (c) an `/account/billing` page that renders the pilot ribbon and the refund CTA. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 commits the webhook handler (`BillingWebhookService::_on_checkout_completed`) as the load-bearing surface that mints the user + subscription rows and triggers the magic-link mint; the success surface depends on the webhook handler having committed the rows before the buyer hits `/account/billing`. The observed surface (cookied buyer, but no subscription on file) is consistent with either (i) the webhook handler 500'd silently (but Commit 3e + 3f already proved the webhook path is solid post-Python-3.14 dict-conversion fix), (ii) the webhook handler succeeded but the marketing site's session cookie was minted from a different code path that does not require subscription presence (e.g., a returning-user cookie from a prior session that never had a subscription), (iii) the webhook handler succeeded but the buyer's email was normalized differently on the website-side `/me` lookup than on the backend-side subscription write, or (iv) a webhook race — the buyer arrived at `/account/billing` before the webhook had committed.
**Repo state:** Backend on `main` at `43b2614`, live at `luciel-backend:59`. No code change made today; the observed surface is a runtime question, not a code-change question. The advisor did not get to inspect the DB row or the CloudWatch logs for the buyer email before the pivot to GATE 5 — the diagnostic was attempted four times via `aws ecs execute-command` and each attempt was broken by PowerShell argument splitting on the multi-line / semicolon-containing `python -c` payload (see `D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16`). The closest in-flight artifact is the user's screen capture `image.jpg` shared in chat (not in the workspace).
**Operational impact today:** Medium-high if reproducible. The marketing-site Account page is the customer-facing landing surface for the pilot journey; if a real customer signs up, pays $100 CAD, and lands on "NO SUBSCRIPTION ON FILE" they have no path forward without contacting support. Magic-link email absence is even worse: the customer has paid but cannot log in. Mitigation today (without closure of this drift): the on-page Stripe receipt email plus the Stripe Dashboard refund path remain available, so the customer's money can be returned manually; but this is exactly the operator-mediated path Step 30a.2-pilot was designed to retire. The 2026-05-16 Step 2.1 redo buyer (`aryans.www+pilot-smoke-20260516a@gmail.com`) is the advisor's plus-addressed test account, not a real customer, so no real customer was harmed; if the surface reproduces on a real customer signup before this drift closes, the impact escalates immediately.
**Owning roadmap step:** Next billing-touch step (likely Step 30b's first-paying-customer arc, or a dedicated Step 30a.2-pilot-followup before then). This drift is a strict precondition for closing `D-pilot-live-evidence-step-21-redo-and-step-23-deferred-2026-05-16` because the V3 inbox leg of that drift cannot be observed if the magic-link mint is broken.
**Resolution path:** Three-stage diagnostic, then a targeted fix. (a) **DB inspection** — once the ecs-exec friction drift is closed (or via the file-write fallback documented there), confirm whether the user row, the subscription row, and the `admin_audit_log` row for `aryans.www+pilot-smoke-20260516a@gmail.com` exist post-Checkout. Three branches: (i) all three rows present — root cause is on the marketing-site `/me` lookup path (case-normalization, cookie-vs-email mismatch); (ii) user row present but subscription row absent — the webhook handler short-circuited on idempotency or fired but failed silently mid-handler; (iii) no rows — the webhook never reached the backend. (b) **CloudWatch inspection** — `aws logs filter-log-events --log-group-name /ecs/luciel-backend --filter-pattern '"pilot-smoke-20260516a"'` to find the webhook event id and trace it through the handler. Look for the `[magic-link-email]` marker (closes the magic-link-absence question) and any 4xx/5xx response to Stripe (closes the webhook-reception question). (c) **Targeted fix.** Branch on the three (a) outcomes: (i) marketing-site fix on `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` `/account/billing` page's `/me` query; (ii) backend fix on the webhook handler's idempotency or transactional boundaries; (iii) Stripe Dashboard webhook endpoint configuration check (URL, signing secret, event types). The closure evidence is a fresh successful pilot purchase + refund cycle with all five legs green, observable from the marketing site without operator intervention.
**Pattern E:** Diagnostic-first, additive-fix when the root cause resolves. No speculative code changes today.
**Validation evidence:** The buyer's screen capture (`image.jpg`, shared in chat 2026-05-16) is the only artifact so far. DB-side and CloudWatch-side evidence pending the sibling-drift workaround.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2-pilot row (the success criterion this drift's resolution defends); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the webhook + magic-link + `/me` chain this drift surfaces a break in); `D-pilot-live-evidence-step-21-redo-and-step-23-deferred-2026-05-16` (this drift is a strict precondition for that drift's V3 inbox leg); `D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16` (the diagnostic friction blocking the (a) DB-inspection step); `~~D-stripe-webhook-checkout-vs-subscription-field-source-2026-05-15~~` and `~~D-pilot-is-pilot-metadata-driven-2026-05-15~~` (sibling Commit 3f drifts — if the root cause is webhook handler behaviour, those drifts' fixes are the design baseline this drift's investigation starts from).

### D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16
**Status:** OPEN — load-bearing prod-workflow friction. Multi-line `python -c '<payload>'` invocations through `aws ecs execute-command` on the operator's PowerShell session get word-split by the AWS CLI argument parser before the payload reaches the container's shell. Observed mode: 2026-05-16 ≈09:35–09:40 EDT during the Step 2.1 redo Block 2 DB probe, four consecutive attempts to read the user/subscription/audit-log row for the Step 2.1 redo buyer email all returned `command not found` or `SyntaxError` shapes that did NOT match the payload's actual code — indicative of word-splitting at the AWS-CLI layer rather than at the in-container shell layer. Workaround attempts: (i) single-line `python -c ""` with semicolons — broke on PowerShell's own semicolon interpretation; (ii) base64-encoded payload wrapped with `python -c "import base64,sys; exec(base64.b64decode(sys.argv[1]).decode())" '<base64>'` — also broke because the semicolon inside the wrapper's double-quoted string is again interpreted by PowerShell before the AWS CLI sees it; (iii) heredoc-style payload — not supported by PowerShell as a here-string for child-process arg construction in this shape. The path that would work but was not attempted before the GATE 5 pivot: write the payload to a temp file (`/tmp/probe.py`) inside the container via a base64-decode-then-redirect single command, then run `python /tmp/probe.py` in a separate exec call.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.2-pilot Step 2.1 redo Block 2 DB probe, 2026-05-16 ≈09:35–09:40 EDT. Surfaced as direct friction blocking the diagnostic for `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16`.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16 ≈09:42 EDT, after the fourth failed probe attempt. The friction is not a Luciel-code defect (the in-container Python interpreter and the `aws ecs execute-command` path both work as designed); it is a documented gap in the operator's prod-workflow toolchain that this drift records so the next operator does not re-discover it from scratch.
**Design claim:** None directly — this drift records an operator-workflow gap rather than a design-vs-implementation drift in the three-doc sense. The closest design hook is the implicit assumption in every prod-deploy runbook (`docs/runbooks/step-30a-1-prod-deploy.md`, the Step 30a.2-pilot GATE 2 round runbooks, and the in-progress Step 2.1 redo runbook on the advisor side) that ad-hoc DB probes during live diagnostics are a reachable operator capability without significant friction. The friction is real and recurring (it has surfaced at least three times across the Step 30a / 30a.1 / 30a.2 / 30a.2-pilot arc, each time absorbed by switching to a workaround mid-session), so the runbook contract is implicitly stronger than the toolchain delivers.
**Repo state:** No code in `aryanonline/Luciel` or `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` is touched by this drift's resolution. The repo state is the absence of a documented ecs-exec DB-probe pattern in `docs/runbooks/`. Workspace artifacts: the Step 2.1 redo runbook (`/home/user/workspace/step_2_1_redo_runbook.md`) carries the failed probe attempts inline as discovery context.
**Operational impact today:** Medium. Each live-diagnostic session that needs a DB probe loses 5–10 minutes to the quoting dance; in the worst case (today) the friction caused a strategic pivot rather than a resolution. The friction does not block any customer-facing surface and does not introduce a security risk — it costs operator time. The risk that matters: a real customer-facing surface bug (like `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16`) may go un-diagnosed-on-time because the diagnostic toolchain is too fragile to drive from a real-customer-incident posture.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — this is operator-workflow tooling, not a roadmap deliverable. The natural closure is a one-page runbook addition the next time the friction is encountered. The drift stays open as a known-tactical operator gap with a documented workaround, similar in shape to `D-rotation-procedure-laptop-dependent-2026-05-12`.
**Resolution path:** Two-stage. (a) **Documented workaround in the runbook layer (closes the immediate friction):** add a `docs/runbooks/ecs-exec-db-probe.md` page that prescribes the file-write fallback: (1) write the multi-line Python payload to a local file (e.g., `probe.py`) on the operator's machine; (2) base64-encode it (`[Convert]::ToBase64String([System.IO.File]::ReadAllBytes("probe.py"))` on PowerShell, single token, no semicolons); (3) run `aws ecs execute-command … --command "sh -c 'echo <base64> | base64 -d > /tmp/probe.py'"`; (4) run `aws ecs execute-command … --command "python /tmp/probe.py"`; (5) clean up with a third exec call. The pattern reduces the operator's PowerShell-side quoting burden to a single base64 token and shifts all multi-line / semicolon-containing logic into the file. (b) **Tooling upgrade (optional, future):** wrap (a) into a `scripts/prod_db_probe.ps1` helper that takes a `-Payload` parameter naming a local Python file and handles steps 2–5 automatically. The (a) closure is sufficient for the drift; (b) is a polish item.
**Pattern E:** Pure addition of a runbook page and (optionally) a helper script. No application code change. No schema change.
**Validation evidence:** Today's four failed attempts (PowerShell session, 2026-05-16 09:35–09:40 EDT, with the user-pasted broken outputs shared inline in chat) are the live-friction record. Closure of this drift will append a successful DB-probe session using the file-write fallback against the next billing-touch diagnostic.
**Cross-refs:** `D-rotation-procedure-laptop-dependent-2026-05-12` (sibling operator-workflow drift, same shape — prod-workflow toolchain friction that doesn't have a roadmap home); `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16` (the immediate diagnostic this drift's friction blocked); `D-pilot-live-evidence-step-21-redo-and-step-23-deferred-2026-05-16` (the downstream verification gap that the diagnostic friction contributed to deferring); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.9 (the integrations + secrets surface that ecs-exec is the operator-side reach-into-prod tool for); `docs/runbooks/` (the documentation home where the (a) closure lands).

### ~~D-cookie-middleware-billingservice-missing-stripe-client-2026-05-16~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-16 — task-def `:61` deployed cleanly (PRIMARY 1/1, no failed tasks, no DRAINING), running image digest verified `sha256:e7506936ca88bf0958018493d438b1e65e8f8c31b52ca9d7b2858ca7a04e982f`, cookied `GET /api/v1/dashboard/tenant` returns 200 with JSON payload in the buyer's DevTools Network tab (tenant `ind-44608fb7`, 2026-05-16 ≈19:04 EDT). Audit-preserved in §3 with strikethrough per move-to-§5 doctrine; closure stanza in §5.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.2-pilot Step 2.1 redo Block 2 diagnostic, 2026-05-16. Surfaced during the `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16` investigation — the buyer was successfully cookied but every cookie-gated dashboard call 500'd because `SessionCookieAuthMiddleware` instantiates `BillingService` with the SQLAlchemy session but never passes the Stripe client, and `BillingService.__init__` requires the Stripe client for any tenant-resolution path that might touch Stripe (e.g. fallback subscription refresh on stale `subscriptions` rows).
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16, after correlating the CloudWatch 500 pattern on `/api/v1/dashboard/tenant` with the `SessionCookieAuthMiddleware` construction site.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Auth model — cookie→admin-context bridge) commits that a cookied request resolves through `validate_session_token` → `User` → `BillingService.get_active_subscription_for_user` → `tenant_id` and grants the same `("admin","chat","sessions")` permission set an admin key carries. The implicit precondition is that `BillingService` is correctly constructed at middleware-instantiation time; the prod-runtime regression was that the constructor call omitted `stripe_client`, causing the dependency-injection path to fail at first cookie-gated request rather than at boot.
**Repo state:** Fix at commit `9108795` "hotfix(cookie-middleware): pass stripe_client to BillingService" on `aryanonline/Luciel` `main` 2026-05-16. The hotfix patch (`hotfix_cookie_stripe_client_patch` in workspace) modified `app/middleware/session_cookie_auth.py` to construct `BillingService(session, stripe_client=get_stripe_client())` instead of `BillingService(session)`. Image `step30a2-pilot-43b2614-r1` with the hotfix was built and pushed to ECR digest `sha256:e7506936ca88bf0958018493d438b1e65e8f8c31b52ca9d7b2858ca7a04e982f`. The deploy script `scripts/deploy_hotfix_cookie_stripe_client.sh` triggered an ECS rolling deploy that landed task-def `:60` with the **wrong** image digest (the stale `fce1be68...` digest), because of the sibling jq-filter container-name-mismatch drift. The PowerShell one-shot to re-register `:61` against the correct digest was authored on the advisor side and handed to the operator; `:61` deploy is in flight as of the doc-truthing commit.
**Operational impact today:** High for any cookied dashboard caller until `:61` lands. Every cookied request to `/api/v1/dashboard/*` or `/api/v1/admin/*` 500s on `BillingService` construction. The marketing-site `/account/billing` page consequently renders the "NO SUBSCRIPTION ON FILE" surface even when the subscription row exists in the DB — the lookup never reaches the DB because the middleware fails first. This is the load-bearing driver of `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16`'s surface symptom. Once `:61` lands and a fresh cookied request succeeds, both this drift and its sibling close together.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2-pilot (the closing-tag arc this hotfix sits inside). The drift is a tactical-fix carve-out rather than a roadmap-step deliverable; closure is a verification observation, not a build.
**Resolution path:** Verify `:61` running, then hit `https://api.vantagemind.ai/api/v1/dashboard/tenant` from the buyer's cookied browser. 200 + JSON body = green. Append the green observation to this drift's body and wrap the heading in `~~` to close, moving the entry to §5.
**Pattern E:** Targeted hotfix — single constructor-call change in middleware, no schema change, no contract change. The deploy mechanic friction (sibling jq drift) is a separate drift.
**Validation evidence:** Pending. The Step 30a.2-pilot Step 2.1 redo Block 2 CloudWatch 500 traces (2026-05-16 ≈09:30–09:40 EDT) are the discovery-side evidence; the green 200 observation against `:61` is the closure-side evidence.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the cookie→admin-context bridge whose construction this drift hardens); `D-pilot-account-billing-no-subscription-on-file-2026-05-16` (the user-facing surface symptom this drift drives); `D-deploy-script-jq-filter-container-name-mismatch-2026-05-16` (the deploy-mechanic sibling that caused `:60` to land the wrong image and forced a manual `:61` re-register); `D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16` (the diagnostic friction that delayed the original root-cause identification); Step 30a.2-pilot GATE 4 live-smoke runbook (the operator-side runbook this drift's resolution unblocks).

### D-deploy-script-jq-filter-container-name-mismatch-2026-05-16
**Status:** OPEN — systemic deploy-mechanic defect. `scripts/deploy_hotfix_cookie_stripe_client.sh` at line 72 uses a `jq` filter `if .name == "web"` to locate the container definition whose image field should be patched before re-registering the task definition; the actual container name in the Luciel task definitions is `luciel-backend` (verified against `luciel-backend:39+` task defs). The filter silently matches nothing, the `image` field is never replaced, and `register-task-definition` writes a new revision (`:60` in today's case) carrying the stale image from the previous revision. The visible failure mode is that an ECS rolling deploy completes "successfully" (no errors, healthchecks green) but the hotfix code is not running. The same defect very likely lives in every other `scripts/deploy_*.sh` in the repo that was authored from the same template.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.2-pilot hotfix-cookie-stripe-client deploy attempt, 2026-05-16. Surfaced when the cookied dashboard 500s persisted after the deploy script reported success against `:60`; the digest in `:60`'s container definition was the stale `fce1be68...` rather than the freshly-pushed `e7506936ca88bf0958018493d438b1e65e8f8c31b52ca9d7b2858ca7a04e982f`.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16, after diffing `:59` and `:60` task-def JSON and seeing the image field unchanged despite the deploy script's stated intent to replace it.
**Design claim:** No CANONICAL_RECAP or ARCHITECTURE claim is directly broken; this is a deploy-toolchain defect rather than a design-vs-implementation drift in the three-doc sense. The closest design hook is the implicit Pattern E contract that every hotfix lands by a clean code→image→task-def→deploy chain with each link verifiable. A silently-no-op'd jq filter breaks the verifiability of the task-def link.
**Repo state:** Defect at `scripts/deploy_hotfix_cookie_stripe_client.sh` line 72 on `aryanonline/Luciel` `main`. The PowerShell one-shot the advisor authored and the operator ran to recover (re-register `:61` against the correct digest via `aws ecs describe-task-definition | ConvertFrom-Json` + in-place image replacement on `containerDefinitions[?(@.name == 'luciel-backend')]` + `register-task-definition` + `update-service --force-new-deployment`) is the manual workaround. The fix on the script side is a one-line jq filter correction (`if .name == "luciel-backend"`) plus a defensive assert that the resulting filtered set is non-empty before the image replacement attempt.
**Operational impact today:** High but contained. Every deploy script in the repo authored from the same template (the count is unverified — the resolution path includes an audit) silently no-ops the image replacement and ships the previous image under a new task-def revision. The operator's confidence-floor for a deploy completing successfully is broken: a green deploy does not prove the new image is running. Today's incident (the cookie hotfix on `:60`) is the first observed manifestation; future hotfixes will hit the same defect until the audit + fix lands. Contained because the manual `:61` re-register workaround is documented and the operator now knows to verify image digest post-deploy.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — deploy-toolchain hardening is operational tooling rather than a roadmap deliverable. Natural closure on the next deploy-touch step, with the audit + fix as a Pattern E commit on `main`. Pairs with `D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16` and `D-rotation-procedure-laptop-dependent-2026-05-12` as the operator-workflow toolchain hardening triad.
**Resolution path:** Three-stage. (a) **Audit** — `grep -rn 'if .name == "web"' scripts/` and `grep -rn 'jq.*containerDefinitions' scripts/` across `aryanonline/Luciel` and `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` to enumerate every deploy script with the same template defect. (b) **Patch** — in each affected script, replace `if .name == "web"` with `if .name == "luciel-backend"` (or `if .name == "luciel-worker"` for the worker variant), and add a defensive assert immediately after the filter that the resulting array is non-empty (`jq -e 'length > 0'` short-circuit with a clear error message). (c) **Verify** — next time a hotfix deploy runs, the post-deploy step `aws ecs describe-task-definition --task-definition luciel-backend:<N>` should show the just-pushed image digest in the `luciel-backend` container's image field; the verify step is added to the deploy script itself rather than relying on operator-side post-hoc inspection.
**Pattern E:** Pure deploy-toolchain fix — no application code change, no schema change, no contract change. The audit step is non-mutating.
**Validation evidence:** The `:60` vs `:61` task-def JSON diff captures the live-friction shape on 2026-05-16. Closure of this drift will append a successful hotfix-deploy observation where the post-deploy task-def image digest matches the pushed ECR digest, plus the audit summary listing every script touched.
**Cross-refs:** `D-cookie-middleware-billingservice-missing-stripe-client-2026-05-16` (the immediate hotfix this drift's defect failed to deliver cleanly); `D-ecs-exec-powershell-python-c-quoting-fragile-2026-05-16` and `D-rotation-procedure-laptop-dependent-2026-05-12` (sibling operator-workflow toolchain drifts forming the hardening triad); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.3 (Application tier — the ECS service whose deploy mechanism this drift hardens); Step 28 (Operational maturity — the implicit Pattern E doctrine this drift records a breach of).

### D-intro-fee-scaling-to-per-tier-2026-05-16
**Status:** OPEN — design-locked, Stripe-side and SSM-side surface not yet built. The Step 30a.2-pilot GATE 3 surface (2026-05-15) provisioned one Stripe live Price for the intro fee ($100 CAD one-time) and one SSM put at `/luciel/production/stripe/price_id/intro_fee`. The 2026-05-16 design decision (CANONICAL_RECAP §14 + ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13) scales the intro fee per tier: $100 / $300 / $1,000 CAD for Individual / Team / Company. The closure path requires (a) creating two new live Stripe Prices in account `acct_1TX2BmRytQVRVXw7` (one for `intro_fee_team` at $300 CAD one-time, one for `intro_fee_company` at $1,000 CAD one-time, both in the same CAD-only currency posture as the existing six recurring SKUs); (b) renaming the existing SSM key from `/luciel/production/stripe/price_id/intro_fee` to `/luciel/production/stripe/price_id/intro_fee_individual` (or keeping the old key as an alias for backward compatibility during the rollout window); (c) adding two new SSM SecureString puts at `/luciel/production/stripe/price_id/intro_fee_team` and `/luciel/production/stripe/price_id/intro_fee_company`; (d) shipping the `INTRO_FEE_BY_TIER` constant in `app/services/billing_service.py` and updating the Checkout line-item assembly to look up the right intro-fee Price based on the requested tier; (e) updating the `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` refund path to issue the correct refund amount per tier rather than the hardcoded 10000 cents.
**Section that raised it:** GATE 5 doc-truthing pass on Step 30a.2-pilot close, 2026-05-16, after the partner pushed back on the uniform-$100 framing as inconsistent with the tier-as-products doctrine (CANONICAL_RECAP §14 "the tiers exist as separate products and not as seat counts") and the Section 14 monetization shape ($30 → $300 → $2,000 monthly tier scaling, where a uniform $100 intro on a $2,000/month tier is not the same shape buyer profile as $100 on a $30/month tier).
**Raised by:** Aryan (operator) on 2026-05-16 during the locked-plan formation; the partner pushed back on the agent's initial pricing proposal that contradicted the docs ("Luciel is being designed as we know to be domain agnostic and model agnostic. I hope you have read our docs and understand the business?"), and the locked plan committed to per-tier scaling.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 “Intro offer” paragraph (locked at 2026-05-16 doc-truthing commit): intro fee is $100 / $300 / $1,000 per tier, 90-day window uniform across all six (tier, cadence) primitives, once-per-email-ever rule unchanged. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 “Paid-intro trial mechanics” paragraph (also locked at 2026-05-16 doc-truthing commit) commits the `INTRO_FEE_BY_TIER` constant, the three SSM keys, the audit-row `intro_fee_cents` field, and the tier-scaled `refunded_amount_cents` audit row on `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED`.
**Repo state:** No code change yet. `app/services/billing_service.py` today contains the uniform `INTRO_FEE_CENTS = 10000` constant and the hardcoded `refunded_amount_cents=10000` in the `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` audit row. The Stripe Dashboard for `acct_1TX2BmRytQVRVXw7` shows one intro Price (the $100 Individual). The SSM namespace `/luciel/production/stripe/price_id/` shows one intro key (`intro_fee`).
**Operational impact today:** Zero — no Team or Company customer has signed up yet, and the Individual intro flow on the existing $100 surface remains correct for Individual buyers. The drift carries the gap between the doc-truth as of 2026-05-16 and the prod-Stripe surface; it closes when the Team and Company live-Stripe Prices exist, the SSM puts land, and the code change ships.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2-pilot-followup (a small carry-over deliverable) or rolled into the Step 30a.3 / 30a.4 / 30a.5 build sequence — the practical owner is whichever step first signs up a Team or Company customer, but the design-truth shift happens today.
**Resolution path:** Six-stage. (1) Stripe Dashboard: create two new live Prices (`intro_fee_team` $300 CAD one-time, `intro_fee_company` $1,000 CAD one-time) under product family “VantageMind Pilot Intro Fee” (matching the existing $100 Price's product); capture the two new `price_…` ids. (2) SSM: rename existing key OR add three new keys (`intro_fee_individual` aliasing the existing $100, plus the two new Team and Company keys) under `/luciel/production/stripe/price_id/`. (3) Code: ship `INTRO_FEE_BY_TIER` map in `BillingService`; update `create_checkout_session` line-item assembly to look up the right intro Price by tier; update `process_pilot_refund` to emit `refunded_amount_cents` matching the actual tier-scaled refund. (4) Audit-row schema: extend `SUBSCRIPTION_CREATED` audit row to carry `intro_fee_cents` (already permitted by the JSON-blob audit payload shape — no Alembic migration needed); same for `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED`. (5) Contract tests: extend `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_*.py` with per-tier checkout-session shape and per-tier refund-amount assertions. (6) Live-smoke: pilot Team and Company signups end-to-end at the next billing-touch window.
**Pattern E:** Additive on the application code side (new constant, new map, new audit fields); additive on the Stripe side (two new Prices); additive on the SSM side (two new keys, optional rename of the third). No breaking change to any existing surface.
**Validation evidence:** None yet. Closure evidence is the two new Stripe Price ids in the live account, the two new SSM keys present, the contract-test green run, and the per-tier live-smoke green observation.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶272 (the design-truth shift this drift carries); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 “Paid-intro trial mechanics” (the implementation home); `~~D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14~~` (the predecessor drift that locked the uniform-$100 shape; this drift is the next evolution of the same monetization-architecture decision); CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1 T1 / T5 (the acceptance scenarios that depend on the Team $300 and Company $1,000 intro fees being chargeable on the live wire).

### D-marketing-product-boundary-soft-2026-05-16
**Status:** OPEN — brand-and-copy drift. The marketing site (`aryanonline/Luciel-Website`) and the product surface (today `/dashboard`, post Step 32 wave 2 `/app`) share the same `vantagemind.ai` origin, and the design decision at 2026-05-16 is to keep that origin split rather than introduce a subdomain (no `app.vantagemind.ai`, no separate React build). The drift is that the marketing copy on `/`, `/pricing`, `/about` today does not yet reflect (a) the tier-as-separate-products narrative locked at CANONICAL_RECAP §14, (b) the per-tier intro fee scaling ($100 / $300 / $1,000 instead of uniform $100), and (c) the Individual / Team / Company self-serve framing where a buyer can fully onboard without operator help — the current copy still implicitly treats Team and Company as "book a demo" tiers and frames the intro fee as uniform across tiers. The split is a routing decision, but the brand voice and copy across that split is a deliberate decision the doc-truthing pass surfaces as not-yet-aligned.
**Section that raised it:** GATE 5 doc-truthing pass on Step 30a.2-pilot close, 2026-05-16, alongside the locked-plan formation. The partner's framing — "lets also truthify ur docs accordingly beofre we proceed so we have everything documented while also maintaining the discipline and symmetry of our docs" — makes the marketing copy a first-class doc-truth surface even though it lives in `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` rather than `aryanonline/Luciel`.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16 GATE 5, after locking the per-tier intro fee scaling and the zero-founder-involvement T1/T5 acceptance scenarios.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶268 "the tiers exist as separate products and not as seat counts" + the per-tier intro fee paragraph at §14 ¶272 (locked 2026-05-16) + the T1 / T5 acceptance scenarios at §13.1 (sharpened 2026-05-16 to commit zero-founder-involvement language for Team and Company self-serve).
**Repo state:** Marketing site copy on `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` (`src/pages/Pricing.tsx`, `src/pages/Index.tsx`, the headline copy on the Pricing tier cards) reflects pre-2026-05-16 framing. The pricing page surfaces all three tiers but the Team and Company tier cards do not yet expose the "Start 90-day pilot for $300 / $1,000" CTA that mirrors the Individual tier's "Start 90-day pilot for $100" CTA shipped at Step 30a.2-pilot. The site as a whole does not yet narrate the separate-products-not-seat-counts story.
**Operational impact today:** Low — no live Team or Company customer has been confused by the soft framing, because no live Team or Company customer has signed up yet. The risk that matters is that the first Team or Company prospect to land on the pricing page sees a CTA shape that implies "talk to sales" when the product is in fact self-serve, and falls out of the funnel that the Step 30a.4 / 30a.5 surfaces are being built to capture. Closure unblocks the self-serve funnel for Team and Company tiers.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.4 (Team self-serve completion) for the Team tier card refresh + the separate-products narrative; Step 30a.5 (Company self-serve completion) for the Company tier card refresh. The drift is a copy-pass deliverable rather than a code-pass deliverable; the practical owner is whichever step ships first.
**Resolution path:** Three-stage. (1) **Pricing page refresh** — update `src/pages/Pricing.tsx` to surface the per-tier intro fee CTA on all three cards ("Start 90-day pilot for $100" / "$300" / "$1,000"), wire each CTA through the same `/api/v1/billing/checkout` route with the right `tier` parameter. (2) **Index / About copy refresh** — reshape the home and About pages to narrate the separate-products story: an Individual product, a Team product, and a Company product, each priced to the value of the deployment shape it enables, not to a seat count. (3) **Visual hierarchy** — the three tier cards on `/pricing` should read as three peer products, not as small / medium / large of the same product. Pattern E on the copy side: surgical sentence-level edits, not a full marketing-site rewrite.
**Pattern E:** Pure marketing-site copy + CTA wiring. No backend change, no Stripe change (the Stripe Prices for Team and Company recurring SKUs already exist from Step 30a.1; the new intro Prices come from `D-intro-fee-scaling-to-per-tier-2026-05-16`).
**Validation evidence:** Closure evidence is the live pricing page rendering the three peer CTAs + a Team or Company prospect successfully reaching Stripe Checkout from the public pricing CTA without operator intervention.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 (the canon this drift's copy refresh aligns to); CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1 T1 / T5 (the acceptance scenarios that exercise the refreshed CTAs end to end); `D-intro-fee-scaling-to-per-tier-2026-05-16` (the upstream design shift this drift carries forward into marketing); `D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16` and `D-company-self-serve-incomplete-org-building-ui-missing-2026-05-16` (the product-side surfaces this drift's pricing CTAs route customers to); Step 30a.4 / 30a.5 (the roadmap homes).

### ~~D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16~~
**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-16 by Step 30a.3 close — see §5 closure stanza. §3 body preserved verbatim per §6 doctrine. **Prior status (preserved verbatim):** OPEN — backend landed 2026-05-16 (commits `3c89a71` C1-C4 + `d55105c` C5); marketing-site frontend (C7) and live E2E (C8) outstanding. Backend surface implements the **Option B welcome-email mechanic** (locked by partner judgment 2026-05-16, chosen over Option A URL-exchange to eliminate a Stripe-Checkout → webhook race window where the buyer could land on `/auth/set-password` before the webhook had minted the `User` row). The 2026-05-16 locked plan re-scopes Step 30a.3 (originally implicit in Step 32a's broader auth story) to land password authentication as the daily-login primitive with magic-link as the bootstrap-and-recovery primitive only. **Password is mandatory at signup for every tier** — Individual at $100, Team at $300, Company at $1,000 — not opt-in. The Stripe Checkout success page is a passive "Check your email" landing; the welcome email (sent from the `checkout.session.completed` webhook handler post-User-commit) carries the set-password link the buyer must redeem before any cookied `/app` session exists for them. Daily login is uniformly email + password across all three tiers; magic-link as a daily-login primitive is retired by this drift — its only remaining surface is the recovery primitive (forgot-password) and the bootstrap that gates the first-password-set form for both new signups and invitees. The cookie format and Step 31.2 middleware contract are unchanged; the new primitives are additive to `BillingService` / `MagicLinkService` rather than replacing them.
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.3 re-scoping decision, 2026-05-16, as part of the locked plan for all-three-tiers self-serve completion. The partner's framing on the daily-login UX (a returning customer should not have to do an inbox round-trip every session) made the magic-link-only model a friction surface for the Team and Company tiers in particular, because team-scale customers will return daily and the inbox-round-trip-per-session cadence breaks at that volume.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16 during the locked-plan formation. The 30a.3 re-scope was committed in the same conversation that formed the per-tier intro fee scaling and the scope-adaptive shell, as one of the four critical changes underwriting all-tiers-working-today.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.3 row (added 2026-05-16) commits the password auth + magic-link fallback design with the success criterion "a customer who paid yesterday opens `/login` today, types email + password, lands on `/app` cookied — no inbox round-trip". ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 “Auth model” (locked 2026-05-16) names the new `users.password_hash` column, the two new auth routes (`POST /api/v1/auth/login`, `POST /api/v1/auth/set-password`), the `/forgot-password` flow, and the forward-compatibility argument with the existing cookie format.
**Repo state (as of 2026-05-16 post-`d55105c`):** Backend complete. `app/models/user.py` carries `password_hash VARCHAR(255) NULL`; Alembic revision `a3c1f08b9d42` chained on `dfea1a04e037`; `app/services/auth_service.py` exposes `verify_password` / `set_password` / `request_password_reset` (argon2id via `argon2-cffi`, constant-time verify via sentinel-hash fallback, 8-char floor); `app/services/magic_link_service.py` carries `mint_set_password_token(purpose=signup|invite)` + `mint_reset_password_token` + `consume_*` pair (distinct `typ` blocks cross-class replay) + `build_set_password_url`; `app/services/email_service.py` exposes `send_welcome_set_password_email(purpose=signup|invite|reset)` with the stable `[welcome-set-password-email]` log marker; `app/api/v1/auth.py` registers the three documented POST routes; `app/middleware/auth.py` SKIP_AUTH_PATHS includes `/api/v1/auth`; `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py::_on_checkout_completed` mints the welcome-set-password email **in place of** the prior post-checkout magic-link email. Marketing site `/login`, `/forgot-password`, `/auth/set-password` pages are NOT yet built (C7 outstanding).
**Operational impact today:** Medium. Individual customers who use Luciel weekly tolerate the magic-link cadence (one inbox round-trip per session is acceptable on that frequency). The friction sharpens on Team and Company customers where multiple users log in daily and the per-session inbox round-trip is a 5–10-minute speed bump at the worst possible time (a department lead trying to demo Luciel to their team has to wait for their inbox before showing anything).
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.3. The drift is the design-vs-implementation gap that Step 30a.3 closes; the closure commit cuts the `step-30a-3-password-auth-magic-link-fallback-complete` tag and moves this drift to §5 with strikethrough.
**Resolution path:** Five-stage (re-sharpened 2026-05-16 post-Option-B lock: Stage 5 rewritten from URL-exchange to welcome-email mechanic). (1) **Schema** — Alembic migration `a3c1f08b9d42` adds `users.password_hash VARCHAR(255) NULL`; nullable because the webhook commits the `User` row *before* the buyer redeems the welcome email, so a User legitimately exists with a NULL hash for the welcome-email-pending interval. `verify_password` treats NULL-hash users identically to non-existent users via a sentinel-hash fallback so the difference is not observable by timing. **Landed in `3c89a71`.** (2) **Services** — `AuthService` (`app/services/auth_service.py`) exposes `verify_password(*, db, email, password) -> User` (case-insensitive email normalisation matching the webhook's, argon2id verify via `argon2-cffi`, constant-time across all four failure modes), `set_password(*, db, user_id, password)` (argon2id hash + write, 8-char floor enforced via `PasswordTooShortError`, no auto-rehash on cost bump in v1 — tracked as follow-up), `request_password_reset(*, db, email) -> bool` (always-200 contract enforced at the route, internal log records actual outcome). `MagicLinkService` adds two new token classes — `set_password` (claims include `purpose=signup|invite`) and `reset_password` — both 24h TTL, both consumed by the same `/auth/set-password` route, distinct `typ` claims block cross-class replay. `EmailService` adds `send_welcome_set_password_email(*, to_email, set_password_url, display_name, purpose=signup|invite|reset)` with stable log marker `[welcome-set-password-email]`. **Landed in `3c89a71`.** (3) **Routes** — `POST /api/v1/auth/login` (verify_password → mint_session_token → set-cookie; single generic 401 on any failure), `POST /api/v1/auth/set-password` (tries `consume_set_password_token` first then falls back to `consume_reset_password_token`, calls `set_password`, commits, mints cookie; 422 `{code: password_too_short}` on under-8-char, 401 on token failure), `POST /api/v1/auth/forgot-password` (always 200 with generic body, exceptions swallowed and logged). `/api/v1/auth` added to `SKIP_AUTH_PATHS` so anonymous callers reach the handler. **Landed in `3c89a71` + `d55105c`.** (4) **Marketing site** — `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` gets three new pages: `/login` (email + password + "Forgot password" link, POSTs to `/api/v1/auth/login`), `/forgot-password` (email-only, POSTs to `/api/v1/auth/forgot-password`, renders the generic 200 message regardless), `/auth/set-password` (reads token from query string, renders password input + 8-char client-side hint, POSTs `{token, password}` to `/api/v1/auth/set-password`, follows the response `redirect` field to `/app` on 200, renders inline error on 422 with `code=password_too_short`, renders "link expired" on 401). The same page is the shared first-password-set surface for signup (Step 30a.3 Stage 5), invite-acceptance (Step 30a.4 / 30a.5), and reset (this drift's `forgot-password` route). **Outstanding — C7.** (5) **Welcome-email mechanic at Checkout success (the mandatory-at-signup enforcement point)** — partner-locked 2026-05-16 as Option B over Option A. The Stripe Checkout `success_url` remains at `settings.billing_success_url` (a passive marketing-site landing page that reads "Check your email — we've sent your welcome link"); **no token is exchanged in the URL**. Inside the `checkout.session.completed` webhook handler, after the `User` + `Subscription` rows commit, the handler calls `mint_set_password_token(user_id=user.id, email=email, tenant_id=tenant_id, purpose="signup")` and emails the buyer via `send_welcome_set_password_email(purpose="signup")`. The buyer clicks the email, lands on `/auth/set-password?token=<jwt>`, types a password, and the route mints the session cookie + redirects to `/app`. The post-Checkout magic-link email is **removed**, not retained — the buyer has exactly one inbox round-trip in their lifecycle, at signup only. Recovery from a dropped welcome email is via `/forgot-password` against the same email (mints a `reset_password`-class token that consumes through the same `/auth/set-password` route). This eliminates the Option A race window where the buyer could navigate to `/auth/set-password?token=...` faster than the webhook could commit the `User` row, and eliminates the cookie-issuance-without-password-set anti-pattern of the pre-30a.3 magic-link flow. **Backend landed in `3c89a71`; closes when C7 marketing pages ship + C8 live E2E records a paid signup completing the welcome-email round-trip on prod.**
**Pattern E:** Additive end-to-end — new column (nullable), new service, new routes, new pages. The existing magic-link flow is unchanged. The cookie shape is identical, so Step 31.2's middleware contract holds without modification.
**Validation evidence:** Backend contract tests green — `tests/api/test_step30a_3_auth_shape.py` 27/27 pass on 2026-05-16 (commit `d55105c`); `tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py` 54/54 still green (no regression from C4 webhook rewrite). Closure evidence (still outstanding): C7 marketing pages live on `vantagemind.ai`, and C8 live E2E records a paid Individual-tier signup completing the Checkout → welcome-email → set-password → cookied-`/app` round-trip on the prod surface with the audit row tagging `purpose=signup`.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.3 row (the design home); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 “Auth model” (the implementation home — Option B welcome-email mechanic locked there); `D-magic-link-auth-cookie-session-2026-05-13` (the predecessor drift on cookie session shape — stays open through Step 32a's broader auth story; this drift closes the password-fallback + mandatory-at-signup slice only); `D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16` and `D-company-self-serve-incomplete-org-building-ui-missing-2026-05-16` (strict dependents — the invite-acceptance flow is the first password-set event for invitees, re-using the same `/auth/set-password` route with `purpose=invite`).

### D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16
**Status:** OPEN — paid-without-product gap. Today a Team-tier customer who pays the $300 intro fee on the public pricing page lands on `/dashboard` (post Step 32 wave 2: `/app`) and sees their Team-scope dashboard — but has no in-app way to invite the three teammates whose work product the Team Luciel is supposed to draw from. The backend primitive exists (Step 30a.1 commit G shipped the `teammate_email` override on `/admin/luciel-instances` POST that mints a User + Agent + ScopeAssignment + magic-link email), but no UI calls it. A founder-mediated workaround exists (the founder can hit the admin API on the customer's behalf), which violates the zero-founder-involvement bar that CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1 T1 / T5 commit to.
**Section that raised it:** Locked-plan formation, 2026-05-16, alongside the per-tier intro fee scaling and the scope-adaptive shell. The partner's framing — "lets get all teirs working to end to end today" — made the missing Team invite UI a load-bearing gap, because a customer who has paid $300 and cannot invite anyone is a refund waiting to happen.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16 during the locked-plan formation. The gap was visible from the start of the Step 30a.1 close (the backend primitive shipped, the UI did not), but it was rolled into the catch-all Step 32a placeholder until 2026-05-16's locked plan carved it out into its own step.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.4 row (added 2026-05-16) commits the success criterion "a Team customer who paid the $300 intro fee opens `/app`, clicks `Invite teammate`, types three teammate emails, clicks Send. Three invite emails go out through SES. Each teammate clicks the link, sets a password, lands on `/app` with Team scope and their own agent provisioned under the Team's default domain. The department lead sees all three new agents on `/app/team`. Zero founder involvement." ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 “Team-invite path” paragraph (re-locked 2026-05-16) names the dedicated `POST /api/v1/admin/invites` route and the `/app/team` page as the closing surfaces.
**Repo state:** Backend primitive lives at `app/api/v1/admin.py::create_luciel_instance` (the overloaded `teammate_email` field path) and is contract-test-proven via `tests/api/test_step30a_1_team_invite.py`. No UI surface exists on `aryanonline/Luciel-Website`; no `/app/team` page; no `/api/v1/admin/invites` first-class route.
**Operational impact today:** Zero — no Team customer has signed up yet. The drift's impact escalates to high on the first paying Team customer; today it is a precondition gap blocking Team-tier signups from being recommended.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.4. Strict dependency on Step 30a.3 (the invite-acceptance flow is the first password-set event for every invitee). Closure cuts the `step-30a-4-team-invite-ui-complete` tag and moves this drift to §5.
**Resolution path:** Three-stage. (1) **Backend** — `POST /api/v1/admin/invites` (cookie-gated, scoped to caller's tenant, capped at the tier's instance cap), accepts `{email, display_name?}`, mints an invite-token row in a new `user_invites` table (or piggybacks on `magic_link_tokens` with an `invite` claim payload), emits an SES email with subject "You've been invited to <Team name> on VantageMind" and a single-use HS256 token (7-day expiry) link to `/app/invite/<token>`. (2) **Frontend** — `src/pages/AppTeam.tsx` (or the equivalent under the Step 32 wave 2 shell), lists pending and accepted invites, exposes an "Invite teammate" form. `src/pages/AppInviteAccept.tsx` is the landing page for the invite link — first password-set event using the Step 30a.3 `POST /api/v1/auth/set-password` route, then cookied redirect to `/app`. (3) **Audit** — a new `USER_INVITED` action constant in `admin_audit_log` carrying `{invited_email, invited_role, inviter_user_id}` per the §4.3 chain.
**Pattern E:** Additive — new table (or new claim payload), new route, new page, new audit action. The existing `teammate_email` overload on `/luciel-instances` POST is retained for backward compatibility through Step 30a.4 and deprecated thereafter.
**Validation evidence:** None yet. Closure evidence is a live Team customer ($300 intro paid) inviting three teammates from `/app/team` without operator help, all three invites accepted, the three new agents visible to the department lead. This is the T1 leg-3 / T5 leg-2 evidence in CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.4 row (the design home); CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1 T1 / T5 (the acceptance scenarios this drift's closure unblocks); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 “Team-invite path” (the implementation home); ARCHITECTURE §4.1 / §4.7 (the scope hierarchy + three-layer enforcement that the new route honours); `D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16` (strict dependency — invite-acceptance is the first password-set event); `D-marketing-product-boundary-soft-2026-05-16` (sibling drift on the marketing-site pricing CTA that routes Team prospects to this surface).

### D-company-self-serve-incomplete-org-building-ui-missing-2026-05-16
**Status:** OPEN — paid-without-product gap, Company-tier edition. A Company-tier customer who pays the $1,000 intro fee on the public pricing page lands on `/dashboard` (post Step 32 wave 2: `/app`) and sees the three-tier dashboard view from Step 31 — but has no in-app way to (a) create Domains under their tenant, (b) invite department leads to those Domains, or (c) hand a department lead a `/app/team` surface from which they can in turn invite their own agents. Like its Team-tier sibling, the backend primitives partially exist (`AdminService.create_domain`, `AdminService.create_scope_assignment`) but no UI calls them.
**Section that raised it:** Locked-plan formation, 2026-05-16, alongside Step 30a.4 carve-out. The partner's framing made the Company tier's self-serve org-building the load-bearing surface for T1 — a Company admin must be able to build their own org chart inside `/app` without a support call.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16 during the locked-plan formation. The Company tier's gap is strictly larger than the Team tier's because it includes the Domain-creation surface plus the cascading invite shape (Company admin invites lead, lead invites agents).
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.5 row (added 2026-05-16) commits the success criterion "a Company customer who paid the $1,000 intro fee opens `/app`, lands on `/app/company`, creates two Domains ('Sales', 'Marketing'), invites one department lead per Domain. Each lead clicks their invite, sets a password, lands on `/app/team` scoped to their Domain, invites two agents each. Six invite emails total, all green." CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1 T1 (sharpened 2026-05-16) commits the same shape as the Q1 acceptance scenario.
**Repo state:** `app/services/admin_service.py` exposes `create_domain` and `create_scope_assignment` internally but does not expose either as a cookie-gated HTTP route. No `POST /api/v1/admin/domains` route. The marketing-site `/app/company` page does not exist; the org-builder UI surface is unbuilt.
**Operational impact today:** Zero — no Company customer has signed up yet. Like Team, the impact escalates to high on first paying Company customer; today it is the precondition gap that blocks Company-tier signups from being recommended.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.5. Strict dependency on Step 30a.3 (password auth for invitees) and Step 30a.4 (the invite primitive and the `/app/team` page that department leads need once invited).
**Resolution path:** Four-stage. (1) **Backend** — `POST /api/v1/admin/domains` (cookie-gated, scoped to caller's Company tenant, capped at a reasonable per-tenant Domain limit — say 10 at v1, raised on customer demand), accepts `{slug, display_name}`. Re-use the existing Step 30a.4 `POST /api/v1/admin/invites` route with an optional `domain_id` field so an invite can be pre-scoped to a specific Domain. (2) **Frontend — Company admin** — `src/pages/AppCompany.tsx`: lists Domains, exposes "Create Domain" form, per-Domain "Invite department lead" affordance. (3) **Frontend — Department lead** — the same `/app/team` page from Step 30a.4 is now reachable by a department lead under a Company tenant rather than only by a Team-tier admin; the rendering is identical, the route is reached via the lead's cookied session resolving to a Domain-scope assignment under a Company tenant. (4) **Audit** — new `DOMAIN_CREATED` action constant carrying `{domain_slug, parent_tenant_id, creator_user_id}` per the §4.3 chain.
**Pattern E:** Additive — new route, new pages, new audit action. The existing Step 30a.4 invite primitive is re-used unchanged. The Step 31 three-tier dashboard backend is unchanged.
**Validation evidence:** None yet. Closure evidence is a live Company customer ($1,000 intro paid) creating two Domains, inviting two department leads, those leads inviting two agents each — six invite emails total, all green, on the live wire. This is the T1 acceptance evidence in CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.5 row (the design home); CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1 T1 (the acceptance scenario this drift's closure unblocks); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 “Team-invite path” paragraph (re-locked 2026-05-16 — the Step 30a.4 invite surface is re-used here unchanged); ARCHITECTURE §4.1 (scope hierarchy — Domain creation under tenant scope) and §4.7 (three-layer scope enforcement); `D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16` and `D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16` (strict dependencies); `D-marketing-product-boundary-soft-2026-05-16` (sibling drift on the marketing-site pricing CTA that routes Company prospects to this surface).

### D-cascade-marker-doc-claim-vs-active-flag-primary-2026-05-16
**Status:** OPEN — doc-claim drift, behavior is correct. Surfaced 2026-05-16 ≈19:27 EDT during T9 leg 7 cascade verification against tenant `ind-44608fb7`. The DRIFTS §3 OPEN body and §5 closure stanza for `~~D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14~~` both describe the cascade marker as `deactivated_at` on ten layers; the running schema (alembic head `dfea1a04e037`) shows `deactivated_at` on only THREE tables (`tenant_configs`, `conversations`, `identity_claims`) and the cascade code uses `active=False` as the primary marker on every cascade-bearing layer. `deactivated_at` is a supplementary timestamp companion stamped alongside `active=False` on the three tables that have it, primarily so the retention worker can compute the 90-day purge cutoff via the composite index `ix_tenant_configs_active_deactivated_at`. The cascade is correct; the doc just leads a reader to think the primary marker is the timestamp when it is in fact the boolean.
**Section that raised it:** T9 leg 7 cascade verification probe, 2026-05-16. Discovery sequence: a leg 7 probe was authored against the doc claim (`WHERE deactivated_at IS NOT NULL` across ten layers), failed at table 1 (`audit_log` did not exist — the audit table is `admin_audit_logs`), failed at table 2 (`memories` did not exist — the table is `memory_items`), then surfaced that only three of the ten claimed cascade-bearing layers actually have the `deactivated_at` column at all. Reading the `bulk_soft_deactivate_memory_items_for_tenant` source in `app/services/admin_service.py` confirmed the cascade flips `MemoryItem.active = False`, not `deactivated_at`. Reading the migration source `alembic/versions/dfea1a04e037_step30a_2_deactivated_at_and_retention.py` confirmed the design intent: the migration explicitly chose to add `deactivated_at` to only three tables and explicitly chose NOT to add it to `sessions` (status-driven) or `messages` (FK CASCADE through sessions).
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16, after the T9 leg 7 audit-trail evidence proved the cascade fires correctly against `ind-44608fb7` and the per-layer marker probe would have required FK-aware predicates we did not author. The drift exists at the doc layer, not the code layer.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §4.4 ("Every 'delete' operation in production flips an `active=false` flag rather than removing the row") correctly names `active=false` as the primary soft-delete marker. The drift is that the cascade-specific narrative in DRIFTS §3 (line 645 of the OPEN body) and DRIFTS §5 (the closure stanza for `~~D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14~~`) both describe the resolution path as "Alembic migration adding `deactivated_at TIMESTAMP NULL` to `conversations`, `identity_claims`, and `messages` with a partial index on `(tenant_id) WHERE deactivated_at IS NULL`" — a sentence that mis-describes three details of what landed (see Repo state below) and obscures the `active=false`-as-primary-marker fact already correct in ARCHITECTURE §4.4.
**Repo state:** Schema as of alembic head `dfea1a04e037` (production verified 2026-05-16 by `SELECT version_num FROM alembic_version` on `ind-44608fb7`'s tenant DB). `deactivated_at` exists on exactly three tables: `tenant_configs`, `conversations`, `identity_claims`. The cascade-bearing layers using `active=False` as the primary marker: `domain_configs`, `agent_configs`, `luciel_instances`, `api_keys`, `memory_items`, `scope_assignments`, `conversations`, `identity_claims`, `tenant_configs` (9 tables). `sessions` uses `status` (no `active` column). `messages` has neither `active` nor `deactivated_at` nor `tenant_id` — it is scoped purely via `session_id → sessions.tenant_id` FK chain and depends on FK CASCADE for hard-delete (see migration docstring lines 84-99 for the explicit design rationale). The retention-worker composite index is `ix_tenant_configs_active_deactivated_at` on `tenant_configs(active, deactivated_at)`, not a partial index on `(tenant_id) WHERE deactivated_at IS NULL` as the drift body claims.
**Operational impact today:** Zero customer impact. The cascade fires correctly under T9 leg 7's live evidence (audit chain at 23:11:17 UTC against `ind-44608fb7`: `subscription_pilot_refunded` → 5 `cascade_deactivate` rows leaf-first across `memory`, `api_key`, `luciel_instance`, `agent`, `domain_config` → `deactivate` on `tenant_config` → `stripe_webhook` post-arrival `subscription_cancel` + idempotent re-cascade on `memory`, all within 440ms). The drift is purely at the doc layer: a future reader doing a doc-truth audit would walk away with the wrong mental model of the cascade marker.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — doc-correction is a Pattern E prose pass, not a roadmap deliverable. Natural closure on the next active doc-truthing pass that touches the cascade narrative, with the §3 OPEN body of `D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14` and the §5 closure stanza both rewritten to lead with `active=False` as the primary marker and treat `deactivated_at` as the retention-worker timestamp companion on the three tables that have it.
**Resolution path:** Two-stage. (a) **Rewrite the §3 OPEN body of `D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14`** so the Resolution path sentence reads (paraphrased): "Alembic migration `dfea1a04e037` adding `deactivated_at TIMESTAMP WITH TIME ZONE NULL` to `tenant_configs`, `conversations`, `identity_claims` as a timestamp companion to the existing `active` boolean on those tables, plus composite index `ix_tenant_configs_active_deactivated_at` on `tenant_configs(active, deactivated_at)` for the retention worker's nightly 90-day cutoff scan. `sessions` uses `status` (no `active` column); `messages` has no row-level soft-delete marker and depends on FK CASCADE through `sessions`. `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` extended to flip the three missing `active=False` layers (`conversations`, `identity_claims`, plus the existing `tenant_configs` end-of-cascade flip) leaf-first within the same transaction; the existing seven-layer `active=False` cascade preserved unchanged." (b) **Rewrite the §5 closure stanza** with the same correction, plus add a Pattern E note acknowledging that the original closure stanza overstated three details (added column to `messages` — false; partial index on `(tenant_id) WHERE deactivated_at IS NULL` — false, actual index is composite `(active, deactivated_at)`; did not name `tenant_configs` getting the column — false, that is the load-bearing one for the retention worker). Both rewrites land in the same doc-truth commit; both preserve the original body per the §6 "surgical edits only, no version-history sediment" doctrine via verbatim quote-and-correct rather than overwrite.
**Pattern E:** Pure doc-correction — no application code change, no schema change, no contract change. The behavior is correct; only the words describing it are wrong.
**Validation evidence:** T9 leg 7 audit-trail evidence against `ind-44608fb7` at 2026-05-16 23:11:17 UTC (captured in this session). Migration source at `alembic/versions/dfea1a04e037_step30a_2_deactivated_at_and_retention.py` (lines 18, 31, 84-99 carry the explicit design rationale). `bulk_soft_deactivate_memory_items_for_tenant` source in `app/services/admin_service.py` (the `.update({"active": False}, ...)` call is the canonical evidence the primary marker is the boolean).
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §4.4 (Soft-delete by default — the doc-claim this drift defends against being inadvertently contradicted by the cascade-specific narrative); ARCHITECTURE §4.5 (Cascade-correct departure — the symmetry contract whose marker the drift corrects); `D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14` (the §3 OPEN body whose Resolution path sentence is one of the two surfaces the drift corrects); `~~D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14~~` (the §5 closure stanza whose Resolution sentence is the other surface the drift corrects); `app/services/admin_service.py::bulk_soft_deactivate_memory_items_for_tenant` (the canonical code evidence); `alembic/versions/dfea1a04e037_step30a_2_deactivated_at_and_retention.py` (the migration source-of-truth for what columns actually landed); T9 leg 7 audit-trail evidence (the live cascade-fires-correctly proof captured 2026-05-16 19:27 EDT).
