### D-canonical-recap-section-12-row-30a3-bloat-and-candidate-rows-misplaced-2026-05-16

**Status:** OPEN (self-correction, moved to Section 5 in this commit — same-pass-self-correction shape, precedent `D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08`, `D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13` (pass 5), `D-doc-truthing-pass-6-section-3-deletion-on-closure-and-orphan-cross-ref-2026-05-13` (pass 6), `D-canonical-recap-status-cell-bloat-violates-triangulation-2026-05-13` (pass 7), `D-cross-reference-wiring-asymmetric-no-shared-q-step-tokens-2026-05-13` (pass 8), `D-pass-6-mirror-restoration-incomplete-three-deletions-missed-2026-05-13` (pass 9 prior segment)).
**Section that raised it:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 (Roadmap) post-Step-30a.3-closure audit on 2026-05-16, immediately after the partner asked on review of the live $100 paid Individual signup close: *"wait partner before we proceed I am just taking a look at the docs and there are some steps in our roadmap and in all other tables that beleive have not been maintained properly... I also feel there many steps in our roadmap that could probably be merged into one"*. The honest audit answered in three parts: (a) Step 30a.3's just-written Status cell exceeded the ~1500-char triangulation threshold that `D-canonical-recap-section-12-table-overflow-2026-05-14` pins (its initial form held 7,170 characters of closure-stanza prose duplicating the DRIFTS §5 mirror); (b) the row registered as Step "32 evolution" carried a non-stable identifier that could not be greppably wired into the pass-8 Q/Step token graph; (c) two Candidate-status rows (Step 33b "Dedicated infrastructure tier" and Step 34a "Channel adapter framework") carried the "Candidate (build when first customer demands)" / "Candidate" framing inherited from pre-doctrine roadmap entries, which reads as "this row may not be a real step" while the rows are in fact load-bearing architectural homes for cross-refs from §11 (Q1/Q2/Q8 for 33b) and from DRIFTS §3 `D-channels-only-chat-implemented-2026-05-09` (34a's owning step).
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-16, after the Step 30a.3 close was operationally complete on prod (live $100 paid Individual signup completed end-to-end in incognito on `vantagemind.ai` at ≈21:06 EDT 2026-05-16, deploy `b404485` carrying the three-doc reconciliation closure commit). The partner's review-pause question is the operational predicate; the actual breach pattern was discovered by walking §12 row-by-row against the three doctrines in play (§12 table overflow threshold, Q/Step stable-ID token graph, marker-honesty per §6).
**Design claim:** The three-doc doctrine pinned at PR #40 / commit `dfab55e` and the table-overflow doctrine pinned at `D-canonical-recap-section-12-table-overflow-2026-05-14` together require that every §12 row's Status cell answer one question ("is this step shipped / partial / planned, and where is the implementation story") in one sentence + cross-refs, with the implementation prose carried by ARCHITECTURE §3.2.X and the audit-chain detail carried by DRIFTS §5 closure stanzas. Step IDs in the table are the load-bearing handles for the pass-8 Q/Step token graph; non-stable identifiers (`32 evolution`, `30a-polish`, etc.) break the grep contract that triangulation depends on. The 📋 Candidate marker reads as a fourth marker tier alongside ✅ / 🔧 / 📋 / 🔬 but is not part of the §6 marker contract — it is informal shorthand for "Planned with no current ETA" that should be honest about its meaning rather than imply the row is provisional.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `docs/CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §12 carries: (a) the just-landed Step 30a.3 Status cell at 7,170 characters reproducing the full DRIFTS §5 closure stanza for `~~D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16~~` (Pattern E framing, shipped surface, prod state, smoke probe, cross-refs all duplicated); (b) one row identified as "Step 32 evolution" with that exact non-stable label appearing 12 times across §12 + ARCHITECTURE §3.2.12 + DRIFTS §3 cross-refs; (c) Step 33b row with Status `📋 Candidate (build when first customer demands). Hardens Q1 / Q2 / Q8 deployment topology for enterprise customers.`; (d) Step 34a row with Status `📋 Candidate. Operationalises Q7 (channels) and the voice/SMS/email legs of Q8 (cross-channel continuity)...`. The pass-7/pass-8 doctrine grep predicates (Status-cell length ≤1,500 chars; Q/Step stable-ID coverage; explicit marker tier) all fail against this state.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** Zero customer impact and zero behavior impact. Step 30a.3 shipped correctly on prod; the cascade still fires; the auth flow works as designed. The impact is on **read-cold-ness** and **graph-greppability** — the breach is exactly the failure mode the pass-7 and pass-8 self-corrections were designed to catch on subsequent passes. The partner's pause-on-review caught it before pass 9 declared closed.
**Owning roadmap step:** Pass 9 §12 honesty pass (this same commit). Scoped to: (1) Step 30a.3 row migrated to short-form (one sentence + cross-refs into ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 and DRIFTS §5 closure stanza, full content preserved in the DRIFTS §5 mirror); (2) "Step 32 evolution" renamed to "Step 32b" with the rename propagated across §12 + ARCHITECTURE + DRIFTS in the same commit, one grammar-artifact fix ("the post Step 32b of the dashboard surface" → "the follow-on to Step 32's single-shell dashboard surface"); (3) Step 33b and Step 34a Status cells re-stated as `📋 Planned (no current ETA)` with explicit acknowledgement of the architectural-home role each row carries (33b is the §11 Q1/Q2/Q8 enterprise-deployment owner; 34a is the owning step for the open `D-channels-only-chat-implemented-2026-05-09` drift); (4) top-of-§12 ordering note added explaining that rows are ordered by raise date, not execution sequence, with the planned-next sequence carried by §13.1 T-scenarios.
**Resolution path:** Four fixes land in this same commit (pass 9 §12 honesty pass): (a) Step 30a.3 §12 Status cell compressed from 7,170 chars to ≈2,830 chars — one sentence of what shipped + ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 cross-ref + DRIFTS §5 closure-stanza cross-ref + closing tag + the Q-row pointer it satisfies (Q1 self-serve daily-login leg). Full closure-stanza content preserved verbatim in the existing DRIFTS §5 mirror for `~~D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16~~` (no audit-chain loss). (b) "Step 32 evolution" → "Step 32b" renamed at all 12 occurrences across the three canonical docs; one grammar fix in the §12 description column to preserve readability after rename. (c) Step 33b and Step 34a Status cells re-stated from informal `📋 Candidate` framing to `📋 Planned (no current ETA)` with explicit naming of the architectural-home role each row carries — 33b stays in §12 as the Q1/Q2/Q8 enterprise-deployment owner from §11, 34a stays in §12 as the owning step for the open `D-channels-only-chat-implemented-2026-05-09` drift (demoting either row would orphan cross-refs and break the pass-8 token graph). (d) Top-of-§12 ordering note added explaining the table is event-ordered, not execution-ordered, with the planned-next sequence carried by §13.1 T-scenarios.

This drift's §5 closure mirror lands in this same commit per the same-pass-self-correction precedent.
**Pattern E:** No content is destroyed. The Step 30a.3 architectural-and-rollout detail being moved out of the §12 Status cell already lives in (i) ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Auth model — Option B welcome-email mechanic) and (ii) DRIFTS §5 closure stanza for `~~D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16~~`. The pass-8 token graph is strengthened (not weakened) by the rename: "Step 32b" is the greppable stable identifier the graph expects; "32 evolution" was a non-stable label that the pass-8 audit overlooked because the slug was novel rather than mis-tokened. The Candidate → Planned (no current ETA) re-stating is honest marker discipline, not a status downgrade — both rows carry the same operational meaning (no current ETA), but the new framing names that fact explicitly without implying the rows are provisional.
**Doctrine reflection (recorded for future passes):** Pass 6 audited §3/§5 mirror discipline; pass 7 audited Status-cell length; pass 8 audited Q/Step token-graph coverage; pass 9 prior segment audited the audit predicate itself for too-narrow scope. This pass 9 §12 honesty pass adds a fifth audit shape: **marker-tier honesty**. The pattern: an informal marker tier ("Candidate", "Polish", "Future") added to a §12 row may carry legitimate semantic meaning at the time it was raised, but reads to a cold reviewer as "this row may not be a real step" — which is exactly wrong for rows that are architectural homes for live cross-refs from §11 or DRIFTS §3. Future closing passes should walk every Status cell's marker against the four canonical markers §6 names (✅ 🔧 📋 🔬) and either re-state any informal marker tier in canonical terms ("📋 Planned (no current ETA)" is the canonical home for what used to be called Candidate) or, if the row genuinely is not a real step, demote it out of §12. The audit predicate: for every §12 row, the marker must be one of the four canonical markers, and any qualifier ("no current ETA", "build when first customer demands") must read as honest scheduling state rather than as marker-tier ambiguity. The partner's review-pause question is also the meta-doctrinal observation worth recording: **operator review can catch what the agent's own audit predicates miss, because the operator carries the read-cold contract in their actual reading of the docs, not in a grep**. Future passes should treat partner-review pauses on §12 as the highest-signal audit input available, even when the agent's grep predicates report clean.
**Cross-refs:** Doctrine pins: CANONICAL_RECAP §16 (read-cold contract), DRIFTS §1 (three-doc doctrine), §6 (marker contract / move-to-§5 discipline). Prior table-overflow drift this pass operationalises against the Step 30a.3 row: `D-canonical-recap-section-12-table-overflow-2026-05-14`. Same-pass-self-correction precedents: `D-canonical-recap-q1-q8-roadmap-genericized-2026-05-08`, `D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13`, `D-doc-truthing-pass-6-section-3-deletion-on-closure-and-orphan-cross-ref-2026-05-13`, `D-canonical-recap-status-cell-bloat-violates-triangulation-2026-05-13` (pass 7), `D-cross-reference-wiring-asymmetric-no-shared-q-step-tokens-2026-05-13` (pass 8), `D-pass-6-mirror-restoration-incomplete-three-deletions-missed-2026-05-13` (pass 9 prior segment). ### ~~D-pilot-refund-customer-email-missing-2026-05-15~~
**Status:** RESOLVED 2026-05-16 by Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3j. Originally raised on 2026-05-15 immediately after the first live $100 CA self-serve pilot refund completed end to end (Stripe `pyr_1TXXwHRytQVRVXw7BGiHdxiJ`, sub `sub_1TXUN1RytQVRVXw7wmsfATXJ`, charge `py_3TXUMwRytQVRVXw70A1iOPs5`). The Stripe-side refund + cancel succeeded, the DB cascade fired cleanly (5-row audit chain `pilot_refund:user:7ad0e573…` + `stripe_webhook` with `row_hash` chain intact across rows 4234–4238), the tenant deactivated (`tenant_configs.id=313`, `deactivated_at=2026-05-16 02:26:52.339805+00:00`), the subscription row flipped (`status=canceled`, `active=False`, `canceled_at=2026-05-16 02:26:56+00:00`), and the website rendered the locked refund-success surface line for line per CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶273 ("REFUND COMPLETE / $100 CAD refunded / Your refund has been issued to the original card and should appear within 5–7 business days. Your subscription has been canceled and your account has been closed in the same step. / Stripe refund id: pyr_… / Back to home / Anything we can do better?"). The buyer's inbox, however, received no email from VantageMind/Luciel. Source-code audit of `app/services/billing_service.py::process_pilot_refund` confirms the handler intentionally has no outbound mail call — the design's customer-communication leg is the on-page success surface plus Stripe's own optional refund receipt (configured in Settings → Emails → Customer emails on the live account `acct_1TX2BmRytQVRVXw7`).
**Section that raised it:** Step 30a.2-pilot Step 2.2 attempt 3 V3 verification (post-cascade email leg). V1 (Stripe Dashboard) and V2 (DB audit chain) were both fully green; V3 (inbox check at `aryans.www+pilot-smoke-20260515b@gmail.com`) returned no mail. The mismatch between the runbook's stated expectation ("a magic-link or refund-confirmation email") and the implementation reality (no outbound mail at all) was traced to a misread of CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶273 by the runbook author; the canon never committed to a courtesy email, but the absence is a customer-experience gap regardless.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-15 22:43 EDT during the cascade verification block on Step 2.2 attempt 3, immediately after V2 audit chain confirmed end-to-end integrity. The partner explicitly chose to file the drift rather than close the gap silently ("lets go with option B partner so we dont foret about it").
**Design claim (current):** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶273 ("Intro refund policy") commits the **mechanic** (full refund anytime in the 90-day window, first-time-only, self-serve, one-click cancel + refund cascade) but is silent on customer-facing communication after the click. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 ("Eight-route HTTP surface" / `BillingService.process_pilot_refund` spec) enumerates four atomic side effects (Stripe Refund.create, Stripe Subscription.cancel, one `AdminAuditLog` row, tenant cascade-deactivate) and does not list email send among them. The post-refund email is therefore a **deferred polish item**, not a regression from canon — nothing was promised that has not been delivered.
**Design claim (proposed for follow-up commit):** Add a fifth atomic side effect to `process_pilot_refund` that fires an SES email to the buyer's `customer_email` (the address Stripe captured at checkout, which is the same address the buyer used to sign up) summarizing the refund. Suggested template payload: subject "Your VantageMind pilot has been refunded"; body containing the refunded amount in CAD, the Stripe refund id (for the buyer's records), confirmation that the subscription has been canceled and the account closed in the same step, the 5–7 business day expected card-credit window, and a single CTA "Tell us what we could have done better" linking to a survey URL (or the existing `mailto:` on the success surface as a stopgap). The email send must be **best-effort**: a SES failure must not roll back the refund, the cancel, or the cascade — the customer has been made whole financially and the audit row is the source of truth. A SES failure should log loudly (the existing `stripe_webhook` logger pattern) and write a follow-up audit row with `action='pilot_refund_email_send_failed'` so an operator can manually retry. This is the same idempotency posture the webhook handlers already use against Stripe.
**Operational impact today:** Low. The on-page success surface is the customer-facing receipt; Stripe's optional account-level refund email (if enabled in Dashboard → Settings → Emails) covers the financial-receipt leg from the payments provider's side. The gap is a polish item, not a doctrine violation. The two adjacent risks to monitor: (a) a buyer who clicks refund and immediately closes the browser tab has no record of the Stripe refund id without going back to Stripe Dashboard — the operator-side audit chain has it but the customer does not; (b) a buyer with auto-archiving inbox rules who never sees the Stripe-side refund email has no out-of-band confirmation that the refund actually fired. Both are uncommon edges; neither blocks the closing tag.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2-pilot follow-up (out of scope for the closing tag `step-30a-2-pilot-complete`; in scope for the next billing-touch step, likely Step 30b or a dedicated Step 30a.3-polish if scheduled before then).
**Resolution sketch:** New helper `BillingService._send_refund_email(*, customer_email: str, refund_id: str, amount_cents: int, currency: str)` in `app/services/billing_service.py`. Implementation calls the existing SES-backed email client (the one that mints magic-links on signup — same code path, same verified sender). Template lives in `app/templates/email/pilot_refund.html` (HTML body) and `pilot_refund.txt` (plaintext fallback per SES best practice). Helper is called from `process_pilot_refund` AFTER the `self.db.commit()` succeeds, wrapped in `try/except Exception: logger.exception(…)`. The handler still returns the same `{refund_id, charge_id, refunded_amount_cents, currency}` dict to the route layer; email failures do not surface to the customer (their on-page success surface already shipped). Regression tests in `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_refund_email.py` (TBD on follow-up): handler calls `_send_refund_email` exactly once with the right kwargs; SES failure does not roll back the refund; SES failure writes a `pilot_refund_email_send_failed` audit row; template renders the four required fields.
**Pattern E:** Pure addition of a fifth side effect post-commit. New code path; no existing call site mutated; no schema change; no SDK pin change; no contract change to the route layer or the response shape. Handler return value unchanged.
**Validation evidence:** Live evidence of the gap from 2026-05-15 V3 verification: buyer inbox `aryans.www+pilot-smoke-20260515b@gmail.com` received no mail in the 15 minutes after refund completion at 02:26:56 UTC. Source audit of `process_pilot_refund` (lines 476–700 of `app/services/billing_service.py` as of commit `113d4d9`) showed no `email`, `magic`, `send`, `notify`, `ses` call inside the handler. **Closure evidence (Commit 3j, 2026-05-16):** `app/services/email_service.py` now exposes `send_pilot_refund_email(*, to_email, refund_id, amount_cents, currency, display_name=None)` and `RefundEmailError`, mirroring the prod-proven `send_magic_link_email` SES v2 transport path used by the magic-link mint earlier in this arc. `app/services/billing_service.py::process_pilot_refund` now calls the helper AFTER `self.db.commit()`; a `RefundEmailError` writes a follow-up audit row with `action='pilot_refund_email_send_failed'` carrying `{stripe_refund_id, error_class, error_message_truncated, to_email}` in `after_json`, then re-commits. Outer `except Exception` swallows unexpected failures so the refund cascade can never be rolled back by an email-transport problem. `app/models/admin_audit_log.py` defines `ACTION_PILOT_REFUND_EMAIL_SEND_FAILED = "pilot_refund_email_send_failed"` and whitelists it in `ALLOWED_ACTIONS`. The new contract test file `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_commit3j.py` pins all twelve facets (module-level function, kwargs-only signature, subject constant, body fields, exception class, log marker count ≥3, billing imports, helper called with right kwargs, call ordering after commit, try/except wrapper, failure audit row shape, action constant whitelisted) and passes 12/12; full Step 30a.2-pilot regression passes 84/84. End-to-end live proof of mail delivery will land on the next live pilot purchase + refund cycle (Step 2.1 redo on Saturday 2026-05-16) once `luciel-backend:59` is rolled with the Commit 3j image.
**Cross-refs:** Predecessor drift `D-pilot-refund-endpoint-and-website-surface-2026-05-15` (the parent drift that carved out the refund-route and website-surface implementation — this drift is a sub-gap surfaced during the close of that one). CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶273 (refund policy — to be amended on follow-up commit to add the courtesy-email leg). ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — to be amended on follow-up commit to add the fifth side effect to the `process_pilot_refund` spec).

### ~~D-pilot-refund-endpoint-and-website-surface-2026-05-15~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-16 by Step 30a.2-pilot Commits 3a–3j (parent drift of the entire Commit 3a–3j arc). Entry retained in §3 with strikethrough per §6 (move-to-§5 with strikethrough, do **not** delete from §3).
**Closing commit:** Step 30a.2-pilot Commit 3j (`43b2614`) is the closing commit of the arc, building on Commits 3a (docs lock) → 3b (backend `/pilot-refund` route + `BillingService.process_pilot_refund` + `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` action) → 3c (backend `/me` pilot signal + website Pricing/Signup/Nav/Account/LegalTerms intro-offer surface) → 3d (backend CORS + website pricing CTA fix) → 3e (webhook materialisation fix, sibling drift `~~D-stripe-event-dict-conversion-python314-2026-05-15~~`) → 3f `b754d4b` (webhook reads `trial_end`/`status` from Subscription + `is_pilot` driven by metadata alone, sibling drifts `~~D-stripe-webhook-checkout-vs-subscription-field-source-2026-05-15~~` + `~~D-pilot-is-pilot-metadata-driven-2026-05-15~~`) → 3g `014dab2` (refund write-path mirror, sibling drift `~~D-pilot-refund-write-path-trial-end-asymmetry-2026-05-15~~`) → 3h `113d4d9` (basil 2025+ invoice→charge traversal via `InvoicePayment`, sibling drift `~~D-stripe-basil-2025-invoice-charge-traversal-2026-05-15~~`) → 3i `7198d4c` (docs-only drift filing for the deferred-polish email gap, sibling drift `~~D-pilot-refund-customer-email-missing-2026-05-15~~`) → 3j `43b2614` (post-refund SES courtesy email + failure-audit row, closes the deferred-polish drift). Live evidence captured 2026-05-15 to 2026-05-16: first $100 CAD purchase (Stripe refund `pyr_1TXXwHRytQVRVXw7BGiHdxiJ` against charge `py_3TXUMwRytQVRVXw70A1iOPs5`, subscription `sub_1TXUN1RytQVRVXw7wmsfATXJ`) refunded end-to-end with V1 (Stripe Dashboard) and V2 (DB audit chain rows 4234–4238 with row_hash continuity intact, tenant_config 313 deactivated at 02:26:52, subscription canceled at 02:26:56) both green. **Original §3 body preserved verbatim below for the audit chain.**

**Original Status (pre-closure):** OPEN — IN-PROGRESS on Step 30a.2-pilot close. The backend pilot mechanics (`INTRO_TRIAL_DAYS=90`, `is_first_time_customer`, Stripe Option A line-item assembly) landed at the Step 30a.2 doc-truthing commit on 2026-05-14 and are running live in production at task-def revision `:50`. Two pieces remain unimplemented and are what this drift carves out: (a) the eighth `POST /pilot-refund` route that the 2026-05-15 canon amendment to CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶273 ("Intro refund policy") and ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 ("Eight-route HTTP surface") commit to, and (b) the website intro-offer surface across `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` (Pricing, Signup, Nav, Account, LegalTerms) that translates the locked canon into a customer-facing UX.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-15 during Step 30a.2 website-audit triage. The website concern — "the monetization on our website doesn't reflect our actual monetization" — surfaced that Pricing.tsx, Signup.tsx, Nav.tsx, Account.tsx, and LegalTerms.tsx still describe the pre-Step-30a.2 per-tier trial shape ($30/$300/$2000 CAD/mo with 14d / 7d / 7d trials respectively) rather than the locked paid-intro shape ($100 CAD one-time + uniform 90-day trial, first-time-only, full refund anytime in the trial window). The refund-surface gap surfaced in the same conversation: the partner locked "full refund anytime during the period, first-time only, self-serve" as the customer-facing promise, which the existing seven-route billing surface cannot deliver because (i) Stripe's Customer Portal does not natively expose one-time-charge refunds, (ii) the $100 intro fee is a separate one-time charge from the recurring subscription (Stripe Option A line-item assembly), and (iii) the customer-facing promise is "one-click refund + cancel", not "refund only, trial continues".
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶271 commits the paid-intro shape; ¶273 (added 2026-05-15) commits the refund policy. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 commits the eight-route HTTP surface and the `BillingService.process_pilot_refund` spec, including the eligibility predicate (`is_first_time_customer(email)` + `status=='trialing'` + `trial_end > now()`), the cascade behaviour (refund + tenant deactivation in one transaction), the new `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` audit action with its field set, and the four error codes (`not_first_time_customer` 403, `intro_window_expired` 409, no-active-intro 404, Stripe-not-configured 501). The website surface is implied by the marketing-site contract in §3.2.13 ("the marketing site calls only the Luciel backend") and the Step 30a.2 first-time-gate smoke in `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` annotation.
**Repo state:** Backend (`aryanonline/Luciel`): `app/services/billing_service.py` has `INTRO_TRIAL_DAYS=90`, `INTRO_FEE_PRICE_KEY`, `is_first_time_customer`, `resolve_intro_fee_price_id`, and the line-item assembly in `create_checkout_session`; `app/integrations/stripe/client.py` accepts `intro_fee_price_id` and stacks it on the recurring line; `app/core/config.py` defines `stripe_price_intro_fee: str = ""`. The eighth route `POST /pilot-refund` is **not** in `app/api/v1/billing.py`. `BillingService.process_pilot_refund` is **not** in `app/services/billing_service.py`. The `SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` action constant is **not** in `app/models/admin_audit_log.py`. No contract test file `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_refund_shape.py` exists. Website (`aryanonline/Luciel-Website`): `src/pages/Pricing.tsx` still hard-codes `monthlyPrice: "$30" | "$300" | "$2,000"` and `annualPrice: "$300" | "$3,000" | "$20,000"` with per-tier trial copy; `src/pages/Signup.tsx` does not call a first-time-customer probe before rendering tier copy; `src/components/Nav.tsx` has no signup CTA (only `Book a demo`); `src/pages/Account.tsx` has no pilot-refund button; `src/pages/LegalTerms.tsx` §6 (Billing) describes monthly billing without the intro-fee and refund mechanics. No `useFirstTimeCustomerStatus` hook or equivalent exists in `src/hooks/`. The website is at commit `811387c` on `main` (Step 30a.2 Commit 2 — best-effort PIPEDA-aligned legal copy); the backend is at commit `76ed23f` on `main` and deployed live as `:50`.
**Operational impact today:** Medium. A first-time prospect landing on the marketing site sees the pre-Step-30a.2 tier pricing as the headline, can sign up via the existing Stripe Checkout flow, and — because the backend already runs Step 30a.2 Stripe Option A logic — will be charged $100 + a 90-day trial _if_ the `stripe_price_intro_fee` SSM parameter is populated with a real Price ID, or will hit the `resolve_intro_fee_price_id` empty-string fallback and the route layer's contact-sales 422 short-circuit otherwise (see `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13`). Either way, the customer-facing copy does not match what the backend does; refunds can only be processed through operator-mediated Stripe Dashboard action today, not self-serve. No customer who could previously sign up cannot now; the gap is the Step 30a.2 success criterion ("a first-time customer can find Luciel, see the intro offer, pay $100, use the product for 90 days, refund themselves if they want, or convert to recurring on day 91") which is not yet end-to-end demonstrable.
**Resolution path:** Step 30a.2-pilot close (in flight 2026-05-15) lands in three commits. (a) **Backend (Luciel repo):** add `POST /api/v1/billing/pilot-refund` to `app/api/v1/billing.py`; add `BillingService.process_pilot_refund(user)` to `app/services/billing_service.py` with the eligibility, refund-issue, cascade, and audit-emission sequence specified in ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13; add `ACTION_SUBSCRIPTION_PILOT_REFUNDED` to `app/models/admin_audit_log.py`; extend `app/repositories/audit_chain.py` if any new field-set columns are needed (the four-field payload `{stripe_refund_id, intro_charge_id, refunded_amount_cents, currency}` fits inside the existing JSONB `details` column, no schema change needed); add `tests/api/test_step30a_2_pilot_refund_shape.py` covering 200, 403, 404, 409, 501 paths plus the audit-row contract; extend `tests/e2e/step_30a_live_e2e.py` with a `test_pilot_refund_self_serve` harness step. (b) **Backend deploy:** ECR push `:51`, register `td-:51`, force-redeploy, three-flow + pilot-refund smoke against live. (c) **Stripe live + SSM:** create the $100 CAD one-time intro Price in `acct_1TX2BmRytQVRVXw7`, write the Price ID to SSM `/luciel/production/stripe_price_intro_fee` (closes the parallel drift `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` for the seventh Price). (d) **Website (Luciel-Website repo):** Pricing.tsx replaces the tier-headline price with `"$100 for 90 days, then $X/mo"` plus footnote (first-time customers, refund anytime in the trial), Signup.tsx detects first-time vs returning and shows the matching copy + invokes the right backend path, Nav.tsx gets a `Start 90-day pilot` CTA pointing to `/pricing`, Account.tsx renders a `Refund my $100 intro fee` button when the cookied user is in an active intro trial and wires it to `POST /pilot-refund`, LegalTerms.tsx §6 (Billing) gets a fourth subsection on the intro fee and refund window. (e) **Amplify rebuild + CloudFront `/*` invalidation.** Acceptance: the GATE 4 rewrite covers pilot purchase, Stripe test-clock day-91 conversion, self-serve refund (one real $100 live smoke), repeat-customer block, magic-link, widget embed, and cancel cascade end-to-end. Closing tag: `step-30a-2-pilot-complete`.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row; CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ¶271 (paid-intro shape) and ¶273 (refund policy); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (eight-route surface and `process_pilot_refund` spec); DRIFTS §3 `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` (the parallel deploy gap for the seventh Stripe Price — closes in the same commit arc); DRIFTS §5 `~~D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14~~` (the design-side closure that this drift's implementation now delivers end-to-end).

The partner's binding instruction *"I would leave the judgment onto you partner"* greenlit the agent to execute the merge by its own judgement after Option 3's audit was presented.
**Design claim:** The three-doc doctrine pinned at PR #40 / commit `dfab55e` and the table-overflow doctrine pinned at `D-canonical-recap-section-12-table-overflow-2026-05-14` together require that every §12 row name **exactly one architectural concern** — if two rows describe waves of the same surface with the same backend powering both and a single architectural-home subsection in ARCHITECTURE §3.2.X, they should merge into one row with wave-1 / wave-2 markers, not stay as two rows that read as two independent steps. The greppable stable identifier discipline pinned at `D-cross-reference-wiring-asymmetric-no-shared-q-step-tokens-2026-05-13` requires that cross-references into §12 use stable identifiers; when a row merges, the cross-references must be updated to name the merged row (e.g. "Step 32 wave 2") rather than the now-defunct sibling identifier ("Step 32b").
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `docs/CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §12 carries 26 rows after the pass-9 closing commit `a7484b6` (sorted by step number after `496dc2d`), with Step 32 and Step 32b as two adjacent rows describing waves 1 and 2 of the same `/dashboard` → `/app` shell evolution. Both rows cross-reference ARCHITECTURE §3.2.12 (Step 32b's wave-2 stanza) and §3.2.13 (the shared cookie middleware), both rows describe the same Step 31 dashboard backend, and both rows commit to the same `vantagemind.ai` origin (no subdomain split). The merge candidate is unambiguous; the sibling rows under audit (30a.2 + 30a.2-pilot, 30a.4 + 30a.5, 34 + 34a) each carry distinct markers, distinct closing tags, or distinct drift carriers.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** Zero customer impact and zero behavior impact. The architecture is unchanged; the merge is a doc-truth restatement that names what the rows already describe — a single dashboard-shell concern shipped in two waves. The impact is on **read-cold-ness** and **doctrine consistency** — a cold reviewer reading §12 should see one row per architectural concern, not two rows that read as two independent steps when they are the same concern in two ship windows.
**Owning roadmap step:** Pass 9 §12 honesty pass (Option 3 merge follow-up — this same commit). Scoped to: (1) Step 32 + Step 32b §12 rows merged into a single Step 32 row that carries both wave 1 (✅ shipped, `/dashboard`, commit `4f2d64c`, closing tag `step-32-admin-dashboard-ui-complete` already cut on the doc-truthing commit) and wave 2 (📋 Planned, `/app/*` scope-adaptive shell, planned closing tag `step-32-scope-adaptive-app-shell-complete`); (2) cross-references into Step 32b updated to "Step 32 wave 2" in CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1 T1/T2 (the acceptance scenarios), ARCHITECTURE §3.2.12 (the wave-2 stanza subsection title and the trailing design-claim sentence) and §3.2.13 (the team-invite path's `/app` post-Step-32b annotation), and DRIFTS §3 open drifts at lines 138/164/171/177 (the four open drifts that referenced Step 32b as a milestone); (3) historical-record meta-drift body (`D-canonical-recap-section-12-row-30a3-bloat-and-candidate-rows-misplaced-2026-05-16` in §3 and §5) deliberately preserved as-of-time-of-raise — the prior pass renamed `32 evolution` → `32b`, which was the right call at that moment; this pass merges `32b` into `32`, which is the right call at this moment. This Option 3 merge follow-up adds a sixth: **merge-vs-split honesty**. Predicate: for every adjacent pair of §12 rows, ask whether they describe (i) two independent architectural concerns (keep as two rows) or (ii) two waves / phases / increments of the same architectural concern (merge into one row with wave markers). The signal is the cross-reference shape: if both rows cross-reference the *same* ARCHITECTURE §3.2.X subsection and *the same* backend services, they almost certainly describe one concern in two ship windows. Future passes reading §12 will see a row that names two waves and can grep this drift to learn why; without this drift, the merge looks like a doctrine breach at first read (one row claiming two markers). This is the same precedent the pass-9 §12 honesty pass already established for the rename + marker re-stating: the meta-drift exists so the next reader of §12 understands the prior decisions without re-deriving them.

### D-channels-only-chat-implemented-2026-05-09

### D-scope-assignments-history-table-missing-2026-05-09

**Status:** RESOLVING THIS PASS — closes in commit (b) of this reconciliation
**Raised by:** Architecture §4.3 lists `scope_assignments_history` as one of three append-only tables that matter most.
**Repo state:** `app/models/scope_assignment.py` exists; the model docstring describes append-on-change discipline ("create a new one. Two rows in history, never UPDATE in place") using the same `scope_assignments` table as an append-only log. There is no separate `scope_assignments_history` table or migration anywhere in `alembic/versions/` or `app/models/`.
**Resolution:** The design is option (a) — `scope_assignments` is itself the append-only history. The architecture doc was wrong to imply a separate table. Fix Architecture §4.3 to describe the append-on-change pattern explicitly, removing the separate-table claim. Code is correct; doc was wrong.

### D-celery-task-surface-thin-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN — partially tracked against existing roadmap; retention purge is the load-bearing gap
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.2.4 (background workers handle "ingesting documents the customer uploaded, refreshing search indexes, sending follow-up emails, running scheduled retention purges, and similar")
**Repo state:** `app/worker/tasks/` contains only `memory_extraction.py`. Document ingestion is built but as foreground code (`app/knowledge/ingestion.py`), not a worker task. There is no search-index refresh task, no follow-up-email task, no scheduled retention-purge task. `app/policy/retention.py` defines the policy; the worker that runs it does not exist.
**Owning roadmap mapping:** Document ingestion-as-worker and follow-up emails are subsumed by Step 34 (workflow actions). **Retention purge is not currently on the roadmap** and it is the load-bearing gap because Architecture §4.4's soft-delete + scheduled-purge guarantee depends on it actually running. Without a running purge worker, soft-deleted rows accumulate forever and the storage-cost story in §4.4 ("the retention worker handles that") is fiction.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** Architecture §3.2.4 gets per-responsibility markers (✅ memory extraction, 🔧 document ingestion as foreground, 📋 the rest). The retention-purge gap is escalated to its own drift token below (`D-retention-purge-worker-missing-2026-05-09`) because it has a load-bearing guarantee depending on it.

### D-context-assembler-thin-2026-05-09

**Status:** OPEN — code-quality drift, no owning roadmap step yet
**Raised by:** Architecture §4.2 ("at runtime, both layers are composed in a single foundation-model context, with the Soul layer placed structurally so it cannot be overridden by injected Profession-layer content")
**Repo state:** `app/runtime/context_assembler.py` produces a 6-line prompt: identity + tenant id + domain id + channel + user message + a stock instruction. The actual production prompt assembly happens in `app/services/chat_service.py` and is more substantive than the assembler suggests, but is not consolidated. Specifically missing: per-scope Profession-layer loading as a coherent step, a structural Soul-vs-Profession separation that prevents prompt injection from overriding Soul rules, and an output-side policy check that catches a model attempting to violate Soul-layer rules.
**Owning roadmap mapping:** None today. This is a refactor + a small policy addition, not a feature, so it does not naturally belong to one of the existing roadmap steps. Best fit is as a prerequisite of Step 33 (evaluation framework) since evaluation needs a single observable assembly point. Defer assignment; track as a code-quality drift.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** Architecture §4.2 gets a 🔧 marker. The drift stays open as a known refactor with no scheduled date — flagged for a future roadmap-grooming pass.
