### D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14 by Step 30a.2 — see §5 close entry. §3 body preserved verbatim per §6 doctrine.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-14 during the Step 30a.2 cascade-completion design review. Discovery sequence: the Step 30a.2 design plan called for a `run_retention_purge` worker task that hard-deletes a tenant after its 90-day retention window; walking the dependency graph forward exposed that `AdminService.deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` (which the Stripe `customer.subscription.deleted` webhook calls per §3.2.13 "Pattern E on cancel") only flipped seven of the ten scope-bearing layers below a tenant. The three missing layers — `conversations`, `identity_claims`, and `messages` — had no `deactivated_at` column and no soft-delete pass at cancel time. A retention purge worker built on top of that cascade would have left orphan rows behind on hard delete, breaking the FK ON DELETE RESTRICT contract on `conversations.tenant_id` and `identity_claims.tenant_id`. The cascade gap was load-bearing for the retention worker, not optional polish.
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §4.4 ("Every 'delete' operation in production flips an `active=false` flag rather than removing the row") and §4.5 ("the cascade flips `active=false` atomically across every dependent resource at and below" a deactivated scope) jointly require that **every** scope-bearing row under a deactivated tenant transitions to a soft-deleted state in the same transaction as the tenant flip. CANONICAL_RECAP T11 ("Within one atomic operation, every Luciel for that brokerage stops responding, every key they had is revoked, every department and individual under them loses access, and a full audit record is generated") states the same contract in customer-observable language. The pre-30a.2 cascade satisfied the contract for `domain_configs`, `agent_configs`, `luciel_instances`, `api_keys`, `memories`, `sessions`, and `scope_assignments` (7 layers); it did not for `conversations`, `identity_claims`, and `messages` (3 layers). The contract was load-bearing but not fully implemented.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `app/services/admin_service.py::deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` walked seven tables. `Conversation`, `IdentityClaim`, and `Message` models carried no `deactivated_at` column. The Step 24.5c migration `3dbbc70d0105` (which introduced `conversations` and `identity_claims`) did not include them in any soft-delete shape — at the time of Step 24.5c the cancellation flow had not yet reached production, so the gap was latent. Step 30a's cancel path was the first time the cascade became load-bearing on prod, and even then the gap stayed invisible because no live cancellation had run end-to-end (Stripe live-mode activation deferred per `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13`).
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** Zero customer impact today (no live cancellations have run on prod). High the moment the first real cancellation flows through the webhook: orphan `conversations` / `identity_claims` rows would persist past tenant deactivation, the cross-session retriever would surface them to any other tenant that happened to share an email-derived identity claim (the unique constraint `uq_identity_claims_type_value_scope` scopes by `tenant_id` so the leak is bounded but not zero), and the retention worker — when it ran — would refuse to hard-delete the tenant because the FK ON DELETE RESTRICT on `conversations.tenant_id` would block the parent row delete until the children were resolved.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2 (Paid-intro trial + cascade completion + retention worker). The cascade gap closes in the same commit as the retention worker lands, because the worker depends on the cascade completing first (leaf-first delete order: `messages` → `identity_claims` → `conversations` → `sessions` → other leaves → tenant).
**Resolution path:** Alembic migration adding `deactivated_at TIMESTAMP NULL` to `conversations`, `identity_claims`, and `messages` with a partial index on `(tenant_id) WHERE deactivated_at IS NULL` for the active-row lookups the cross-session retriever and the dashboard rollups perform; `deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` extended to flip the three new layers leaf-first within the same transaction; the existing seven-layer cascade preserved unchanged. `messages` scoping is via `session_id` FK CASCADE (messages have no `tenant_id` column of their own — the FK chain `messages.session_id → sessions.id → sessions.tenant_id` carries scope), so the soft-delete pass walks the tenant's session ids and flips messages by `session_id IN (...)`. Audit row emitted via the existing `before_flush` listener path — no new audit-action constant needed because the cascade is a single logical event (tenant deactivation) regardless of how many rows it touches.
**Pattern E:** No row mutation, no destructive operation. Three additive columns + one additive index. Existing rows backfill cleanly as `deactivated_at IS NULL` (the active state). The cascade extension only writes timestamps it never wrote before; pre-existing soft-deleted rows are not retroactively touched.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — "Pattern E on cancel" subsection, the call-site this drift defends); ARCHITECTURE §4.4 (Soft-delete by default — the design contract this drift closes against); ARCHITECTURE §4.5 (Cascade-correct departure — the symmetry contract); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row (the closing step); CANONICAL_RECAP T11 (the customer-observable contract); `D-retention-purge-worker-missing-2026-05-09` (sibling drift closing in the same commit — the cascade gap was a prerequisite for the worker landing); `D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14` (sibling drift, Step 30a.2 design partner — the trial-policy work is the user-facing half of the same step).

### D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14 by Step 30a.2 — see §5 close entry. §3 body preserved verbatim per §6 doctrine.
**Raised by:** Aryan (operator) on 2026-05-14 during the Step 30a.2 trial-policy design conversation. The pre-30a.2 trial shape (Individual monthly 14d, Team / Company monthly 7d, every annual SKU 0d) had landed at Step 30a.1 (CANONICAL_RECAP §14 "Annual cadence shape" paragraph) as a compromise for the single-SKU Individual flow that Step 30a originally shipped — it was carried forward into the six-SKU Step 30a.1 surface without re-litigation because the marketing-side smoke had not yet run. Aryan's framing on 2026-05-14: "the trial story needs to be the same story regardless of tier and cadence — and a card-required free trial is not actually a trial, it's a delayed bill with an unlock period." Reopening the policy at Step 30a.2 turns the trial from a per-tier feature toggle into a uniform paid-intro offer: $100 CAD one-time at signup + 90-day trial on the recurring price, identical across all six (tier, cadence) primitives, gated to first-time-ever customers by case-insensitive email lookup against the historical customers table.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 ("Each tier ships in two cadences — monthly and annual") and the Step 30a.1 success-criterion row in §12 ("A new Team customer can find Luciel on our website, choose monthly or annual, pay") jointly imply a uniform monetization shape across the six primitives. The pre-30a.2 trial policy violated that uniformity in two ways: (a) Individual customers got more trial time than Team / Company customers, which inverts the value-density story (higher-tier customers committing more money got less time to evaluate); (b) annual customers got no trial at all, which made the monthly/annual choice a different product decision rather than a billing-cadence choice. The locked Step 30a.2 design — $100 CAD intro + 90 days uniform — restores the uniformity and replaces the trial-vs-no-trial decision with a first-time-vs-repeat decision that is observable to the customer ("you've signed up before; the intro offer doesn't apply") and recorded in the audit chain.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `app/services/billing_service.py` carried `TRIAL_DAYS = {("individual","monthly"): 14, ("team","monthly"): 7, ("company","monthly"): 7, ("individual","annual"): 0, ("team","annual"): 0, ("company","annual"): 0}` and applied it via `subscription_data.trial_period_days` on the Stripe Checkout session creation. `app/core/config.py` carried six `stripe_price_*` settings (no intro-fee Price). No first-time-customer gate existed — every checkout was treated identically regardless of the customer's history with Luciel. `app/services/billing_webhook_service.py` did not check the customers table for a prior `stripe_customer_id` against the incoming email before applying the trial. The Stripe Customer Portal configuration referenced the six recurring price-ids only; an intro-fee Price line item would require Stripe Option A (`line_items=[{intro_fee Price, qty 1}, {recurring Price, qty 1}]` in the same Checkout session with `trial_period_days=90` on the recurring Price) to land cleanly in one customer-visible transaction.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** Zero customer impact (Stripe live-mode activation deferred per `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13`, so no real customer has hit any of the pre-30a.2 trial paths). The gap was a design-coherence gap, not a live failure mode. Closing it before the first Stripe live-mode checkout runs is the deliberate sequencing: the trial-policy story locks in *before* the first paying customer hits it, not after.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2 (Paid-intro trial + cascade completion + retention worker). Closes in the same commit as the cascade extension and the retention worker, because all three are deliverables of the same step and the Stripe-side activation (the next operational gate) needs the seven-Price design — six recurring + one intro_fee — to be locked in code before the activation form goes in.
**Resolution path:** (a) `app/services/billing_service.py` — replace the per-tier `TRIAL_DAYS` map with a single `INTRO_TRIAL_DAYS = 90` constant; add `intro_fee_price_id` resolution from `settings.stripe_price_intro_fee`; add `is_first_time_customer(email: str) -> bool` using `func.lower(User.email) == email.lower()` against the historical customers table (case-insensitive match, returns True only when no prior subscription row exists for that email's user); extend `create_checkout_session(...)` to assemble Stripe Option A line items when `is_first_time_customer(email)` is True and to fall through to the recurring-only line item when False (cancel + rejoin = plan rate, no second intro). (b) `app/core/config.py` — add `stripe_price_intro_fee: str | None = None` to `BillingSettings`. (c) Tests — new `tests/api/test_first_time_gate.py` asserts case-insensitive email match and the cancel-rejoin = no-intro path; existing `tests/api/test_step30a_1_tiered_self_serve_shape.py` updated to assert the seven-line-item Checkout session shape on first-time signups and the one-line-item shape on repeat signups. (d) Stripe activation (next operational gate, GATE 3) — seven Prices created in live mode: six recurring + one intro_fee CAD $100; seven SSM puts; ECS force-redeploy; the three-flow smoke from Step 30a.1's runbook extends to a four-flow smoke with one first-time path + one cancel-rejoin path per tier.
**Pattern E:** Live customer rows are untouched. The pre-30a.2 `TRIAL_DAYS` constant is replaced, not deactivated, because it was internal-only application state with no audit-row footprint — the audit chain begins at the Stripe webhook event, not at the trial-policy decision. The `is_first_time_customer` gate reads existing customer rows; it does not write to them. The new `INTRO_TRIAL_DAYS` constant ships as 90 with no per-tier override surface — future per-tier intro variations would land as a new design decision, not as a config flag flip.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 (Monetization — the uniformity contract this drift defends); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row (the closing step); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — extended in this same commit with the intro_fee + 90d trial mechanics); `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` (the upstream operational gate — the seven-Price design lands in code first, then the Stripe activation form lands the seven live Prices); `D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14` (sibling Step 30a.2 drift, code-side partner — the cascade gap closes in the same commit because the retention worker depends on it).

### D-canonical-recap-section-12-table-overflow-2026-05-14

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14 by §12 format migration — see §5 close entry. §3 body preserved verbatim per §6 doctrine.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-14 during the Step 30a.2 doc-truthing scoping. CANONICAL_RECAP §12 (Roadmap) is a markdown table with five columns (Category, Step, Description, How we'll know we're successful, Status). The Status column has been absorbing increasing amounts of implementation detail — closing-tag identifiers, sub-branch enumerations, PR numbers, ECR digests, observed-clean stanzas, the full closure caveats from Pass 8 — to the point where multiple cells now exceed ~1500 characters in length (Pass 7 "surgical edits" threshold). The Step 30a row Status cell (line 192) is 3537 characters; the Step 30a.1 row is 6582; the Step 31 row is 2643; the Step 31.2 row is 5171; the Step 32 row is 4850. Each cell renders correctly in markdown viewers, but the table has stopped serving its purpose: a reader scanning §12 for the business-view answer to "where is the product today" gets pulled into implementation prose that belongs in ARCHITECTURE.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP is the **business view** per the three-doc doctrine pinned at PR #40, commit `dfab55e`, in §16 ("If a chat summary, a session recap, a slide, or a pitch contradicts this document, **this document wins**") and DRIFTS §1. §12 is the business-view answer to the roadmap question; its Status column should answer "is this shipped, partially shipped, or planned, and what's the closing artifact" in one sentence, with the full implementation story carried by ARCHITECTURE's §3.2.X subsection per Step. The current overflow violates the discipline by carrying ARCHITECTURE-shaped content into the business-view doc. Pass 8 already named the threshold ("Status cells > ~1500 characters indicate the implementation story is leaking out of ARCHITECTURE"); Step 30a.2 is the first pass to act on it.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `docs/CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §12, rows for Steps 30a / 30a.1 / 31 / 31.2 / 32 / 30b / 30d each carry Status cells with multi-paragraph implementation detail. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface), §3.2.12 (Hierarchical dashboards), §3.2.11 (Cross-channel identity) all already carry the corresponding implementation story at the appropriate depth — the recap detail is largely duplicative, which is the failure mode Pass 8 named.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** Zero — the docs render correctly and the audit chain is intact. The impact is on **read-cold-ness**, which is the load-bearing property of the three-doc doctrine. A reader opening CANONICAL_RECAP cold today gets pulled into ARCHITECTURE-shaped prose without the ARCHITECTURE framing; a reader opening ARCHITECTURE cold gets the same implementation story but with the design framing intact. The asymmetry breaks the triangulation discipline by making CANONICAL_RECAP harder to read cold than ARCHITECTURE.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2 (doc-truthing pass — the format migration is one of the deliverables). Scoped to (a) the Step 30a.2 row added at this pass, which lands in the new short-form shape, and (b) the Step 30a row touched at this pass for the deferred-Stripe annotation, which gets migrated in place as collateral. Other historical rows (30a.1, 31, 31.2, 32, 30b, 30d) stay in their current verbose shape and migrate forward at the next doc-truthing pass that touches them — Pattern E for prose: rows migrate when their step is next active, not in a bulk rewrite.
**Resolution path:** (a) The Step 30a.2 row lands in §12 with a Status cell ≤ one sentence + at least one stable-ID cross-reference into ARCHITECTURE §3.2.X and at least one DRIFTS slug. (b) The Step 30a row Status cell is migrated in place during this same pass — the deferred-Stripe annotation that was being added anyway becomes a short cross-reference to `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` instead of a multi-paragraph closure-stanza preservation. The original closure stanza is moved to DRIFTS §5 under the existing Stripe drift's resolution path so the audit chain is preserved (no §3 deletions, Pass 9 doctrine). (c) Future rows touched in subsequent doc-truthing passes adopt the same shape — one sentence + cross-refs. (d) No new tooling, no markdown lint, no character cap — the discipline is the doc-truthing reviewer's job, not an automated gate.
**Pattern E:** No content is deleted. The pre-30a.2 §12 Step 30a Status content is preserved in DRIFTS §5 (under `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13`'s resolution path notes) and remains discoverable via the closure tag and the original commit history. The §5 strikethrough doctrine applies to drift closures, not to recap-row format migrations, so no strikethrough is needed on the recap-row migration — the diff itself is the audit trail and `git log -p docs/CANONICAL_RECAP.md` shows the migration cleanly.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 (the section this drift defends); CANONICAL_RECAP §16 (Source-of-truth rule — the read-cold contract); DRIFTS §1 (three-doc doctrine pinned at PR #40); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (the implementation-story home for Step 30a / 30a.1 / 30a.2 billing surface — already carries the detail that's being moved out of recap); `D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14` (sibling Step 30a.2 drift — the Step 30a.2 row added in this format migration anchors that drift's CANONICAL_RECAP cross-reference); `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` (the existing Stripe drift whose resolution path absorbs the migrated Step 30a Status content as preserved audit context).

### D-celery-beat-single-replica-coupling-2026-05-14

**Status:** OPEN — future-debt. Stays open beyond Step 30a.2. Acceptable at current scale (one paying customer, one worker replica); revisit when worker horizontal scaling becomes load-bearing.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-14 during the Step 30a.2 retention-worker deployment review. The Step 30a.2 design ships the Celery beat scheduler embedded in the same container as the worker via the `--beat` flag (Dockerfile.worker injects `celery -A app.worker.celery_app worker --beat --loglevel=info --concurrency=2`). Beat is what enqueues the 08:00 UTC nightly `run_retention_purge` task; the worker pool is what consumes it. Co-locating beat with the worker means running >1 worker replica would duplicate every scheduled tick — two replicas would enqueue two retention purges at 08:00 UTC every night, three replicas would enqueue three, and Celery's lock semantics on the retention task would absorb the duplication safely (idempotency cursor on `tenants.deactivated_at` plus the leaf-first delete order) but the duplicate work would still hit the database. Distinct from `D-celery-worker-runs-as-root-2026-05-11` (which is the root-user gap, not the beat-coupling gap).
**Design claim:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.4 (Background worker tier) commits to "a separate pool of worker processes" with "worker autoscaling on queue depth and CPU" — autoscaling implies >1 replica is a valid operational state. The Step 30a.2 single-replica coupling is therefore a temporary constraint, not a design decision: the design says workers scale horizontally, the current implementation says scheduled tasks fire once *per replica* rather than once *per cluster*. Closing the gap requires either (a) splitting beat into its own single-replica ECS service with the worker pool free to scale, or (b) adding a Celery beat lock (e.g. `celery-redbeat` against the existing SSM `REDIS_URL` for dev or against the prod SQS broker for live) that coordinates ticks across multiple beat-embedded workers. Option (a) is the cleaner architectural shape; option (b) preserves the single-container deploy and is reversible.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `app/worker/celery_app.py` carries the Step 30a.2 beat schedule (`beat_schedule = {'retention-purge-nightly': {'task': 'app.worker.tasks.retention.run_retention_purge', 'schedule': crontab(hour=8, minute=0)}}`). `Dockerfile.worker` injects `--beat`. `cfn/luciel-prod-worker-autoscaling.yaml` exists (and is presumed deployed per `D-prod-worker-autoscaling-unverified-2026-05-09`) — the autoscaling stack's min-capacity is 1 and max-capacity is the GTM-burst ceiling; setting min-capacity > 1 today would activate the beat-duplication failure mode. No celery-redbeat dependency; no separate beat service in CFN.
**Operational impact today:** Zero. Worker desired-count is 1 today and stays at 1 through any plausible single-paying-customer load. The gap activates only when (a) worker queue depth or CPU triggers the autoscaling policy to scale out, OR (b) an operator manually raises the worker service's desired-count above 1 for any reason (e.g., during a deploy when the new task definition is being rolled out and old + new revisions briefly co-exist). The autoscaling policy in `cfn/luciel-prod-worker-autoscaling.yaml` keeps min-capacity at 1, so the deploy-window co-existence is the more likely activation path. Even when activated, the retention task is idempotent (the cursor + leaf-first order absorb duplicate ticks) — the impact is duplicate database load at 08:00 UTC nightly, not a correctness failure.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today. The closure is a Pattern E hardening commit that lands when worker horizontal scaling becomes load-bearing — either when the GTM plan's burst projection exceeds single-replica capacity, or when a second scheduled task lands whose duplication semantics are not idempotent like retention is. Likely natural home: alongside Step 33b (Dedicated infrastructure tier) or as a side-observation commit during Step 34 (Workflow actions, which adds the second wave of scheduled background tasks). Not a roadmap row of its own — the design is correct, the implementation is a known-tactical compromise.
**Resolution path:** Two viable options when this closes. (a) **Separate beat service.** Add `cfn/luciel-prod-beat.yaml` provisioning a single-replica ECS service running `celery -A app.worker.celery_app beat --loglevel=info` (no `--beat` flag on the worker service; the worker pool runs `celery worker` only). Rolls forward via Pattern E: the new beat service comes up alongside the existing `--beat`-embedded workers, then the worker task-definition revision drops `--beat`, then the embedded beat stops firing as old tasks drain. Operational acceptance: worker service min-capacity raises from 1 to 2 (or whatever the autoscaling floor needs); the 08:00 UTC retention tick fires exactly once per night regardless of worker count. (b) **celery-redbeat lock.** Add `celery-redbeat` to `requirements.txt`; configure the beat backend in `app/worker/celery_app.py` to use Redis (or the existing prod SQS broker as a leader-election surface); workers keep the `--beat` flag, but only the lock-winning worker fires ticks. Lighter operational footprint, more coupling complexity. The choice between (a) and (b) is the closure-time decision; this drift records both so the next operator does not re-discover the option space.
**Pattern E:** No row mutation. The closing commit will be additive (new service or new dependency) and the deactivation of the embedded `--beat` will land as a task-definition revision shift, not as a destructive container-config edit. No customer-visible state changes.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.4 (Background worker tier — the design this drift is a known-tactical compromise against); ARCHITECTURE §4.9 (Design choices we deliberately did not make — new rejected-alternative bullet added in this same commit naming the separate-beat-service shape as deferred, not rejected); `D-celery-worker-runs-as-root-2026-05-11` (sibling worker-tier hygiene drift — different gap, same subsection); `D-prod-worker-autoscaling-unverified-2026-05-09` (sibling — the worker-autoscaling stack whose min-capacity matters for when this drift activates); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 33b row (the likely natural home for the closure when it lands); `Dockerfile.worker` line carrying the `--beat` flag (the concrete code surface this drift records); `app/worker/celery_app.py` `beat_schedule` block (the schedule this drift's closure must preserve exactly once per cluster, not once per replica).

### D-vantagemind-dns-cloudfront-mismatch-2026-05-13

**Status:** OPEN — 📋 Planned. Operational drift surfaced during Step 30a.1 prod-deploy planning, not a regression. The marketing site at `vantagemind.ai` is served from CloudFront, but the CloudFront distribution's origin S3 bucket is not in lockstep with the latest Amplify build output — DNS propagation and CloudFront's edge cache combine to serve stale assets to visitors for an indeterminate window after each Amplify deploy. Smoke testing of the Step 30a.1 Pricing + Signup + Dashboard flow against the public `vantagemind.ai` URL is therefore not reliable; the documented smoke-test target during the deploy window is the ALB direct URL (`https://luciel-alb-1617994381.ca-central-1.elb.amazonaws.com`) on the backend side and the Amplify-issued URL (the deployed branch's `*.amplifyapp.com` URL, not the apex domain) on the marketing side.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) on 2026-05-13 during Step 30a.1 prod-deploy runbook authoring. The runbook needs a documented smoke-test target; the apex domain is not it. Discovering this during runbook write-up rather than during the deploy itself is the deliberate "design a business, don't guess" discipline — the operational gap goes into the ledger and the runbook stays unambiguous.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row ("a new individual customer can find Luciel on our website…") implies that the website the customer reaches is the website our deploys actually update. ARCHITECTURE §3.6 (production architecture diagram) names CloudFront + S3 as the marketing-site path. The two together imply that an Amplify deploy → S3 sync → CloudFront invalidation pipeline is in place; today the Amplify deploy lands but the CloudFront origin + invalidation step is not part of the pipeline, so the apex domain serves stale assets until cache TTL expires or until the operator runs a manual CloudFront invalidation.
**Repo state:** No code in `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` triggers a CloudFront invalidation as part of the Amplify deploy. No Amplify post-build hook exists. The CloudFront distribution and its S3 origin bucket are provisioned outside the repo (operator-side AWS resources, no CFN template in `aryanonline/Luciel`'s `cfn/` directory covers them). The backend repo's `docs/runbooks/` does not currently carry a marketing-site deploy runbook; the marketing-site repo carries Amplify-deploy guidance but does not name the CloudFront step.
**Operational impact today:** Medium. A real customer visiting `https://vantagemind.ai/pricing` after a Step 30a.1 deploy may see the pre-30a.1 pricing page (only Individual self-serve, two Pricing cards) for up to the CloudFront TTL window (default 24h with the current configuration). The Amplify-issued URL serves the correct build immediately and is what we use for smoke testing during the deploy; the apex domain catches up when CloudFront invalidates. No customer is *blocked* by this — they can still complete the Individual flow that worked pre-30a.1 — but the Team and Company self-serve paths are not yet reachable from the apex domain during the cache window. The operator-side mitigation (manual CloudFront invalidation after each Amplify deploy) is the v1 control.
**Resolution path:** Pattern E hardening commit on the marketing-site repo that adds a post-deploy step invalidating the CloudFront distribution after the Amplify build lands. Two options, both viable: (a) Amplify post-build hook that calls `aws cloudfront create-invalidation --distribution-id <id> --paths '/*'` using a deploy-time IAM role; (b) GitHub Actions workflow on `main` push that triggers the invalidation after Amplify reports success. Option (a) is more native to Amplify; option (b) is more native to the rest of the platform's CI discipline. Acceptance: a freshly deployed marketing-site change is visible at the apex domain within 5 minutes of the Amplify deploy completing, without operator intervention. Naturally lands as a single short PR with closing tag `marketing-site-cloudfront-invalidation-on-deploy`. No backend change. Cross-cuts the broader "production environment matches the design" question that Phase 2B tracks under DRIFTS §4.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row (the customer-facing surface this drift defends); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.1 row (the immediate trigger — the new tiers need to be reachable from the apex domain to count as "shipped"); ARCHITECTURE §3.6 (production architecture diagram — the CloudFront + S3 path this drift records as needing a closing invalidation step); `docs/runbooks/step-30a-1-prod-deploy.md` (the runbook that names the ALB and Amplify URLs as the documented smoke-test targets during the deploy window); DRIFTS §4 prod-confirmation drifts (sibling pattern — production-side claims whose verification requires operator-side AWS access).

### ~~D-stripe-credentials-never-wired-to-prod-backend-2026-05-14~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-15 by Step 30a.2-pilot GATE 3 sequence (9 SSM SecureString puts + task-def `:46` patch + force-redeploy). Closes together with sibling `~~D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13~~` as a single closure event. Entry retained in §3 with strikethrough per §6 (move-to-§5 with strikethrough, do **not** delete from §3).
**Closing commit:** Step 30a.2-pilot GATE 3 sequence (operational state, not application code): `aws ssm put-parameter --type SecureString --overwrite --region ca-central-1` x9 writing `/luciel/production/stripe_secret_key`, `/luciel/production/stripe_webhook_secret`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_individual_monthly`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_individual_annual`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_team_monthly`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_team_annual`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_company_monthly`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_company_annual`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_intro_fee`; task-def `luciel-backend:46` registered from `:45` with nine new `secrets` entries mapping the corresponding `STRIPE_*` env vars to the SSM ARNs under `arn:aws:ssm:ca-central-1:729005488042:parameter/luciel/production/stripe_*`; `aws ecs update-service --force-new-deployment` on `luciel-backend-service`. Operational verification (post-redeploy at task-def `:46`): the running container's `settings.stripe_secret_key`, `settings.stripe_webhook_secret`, and all seven `settings.stripe_price_*` values resolve to populated live-mode values; `/api/v1/billing/webhook` successfully verified signatures on the live Checkout/Subscription events that delivered after 2026-05-15 18:36 EDT; `/api/v1/billing/checkout` successfully assembled the Stripe Option A intro_fee + recurring line items and redirected the first live $100 CAD buyer to a `cs_live_*` Checkout session. **Original §3 body preserved verbatim below for the audit chain.**

**Original Status (pre-closure):** OPEN — discovered during Step 30a.2 GATE 3 Stripe activation SSM walkthrough. The Stripe-live-activation drift (`D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13`) named the missing Prices + SSM puts as the closure path, but the actual prod state is broader: **no Stripe credential of any kind has ever been wired to the prod backend container.** This is a pre-existing documentation drift surfaced by the activation walkthrough, not a regression introduced by Step 30a.2.
**Raised by:** Computer (advisor) and Aryan (operator) on 2026-05-14 during the Step 30a.2 GATE 3 walkthrough. Discovery sequence: after Stripe activation cleared ("No active tasks for your account" on the Account status panel), the SSM-put planning step ran two verification commands against the live prod stack: (a) `aws ecs describe-task-definition --task-definition luciel-backend:45 --query "taskDefinition.containerDefinitions[0].[environment[].name, secrets[].name]"` returned `[["MEMORY_EXTRACTION_ASYNC","CELERY_BROKER_URL","AWS_REGION"],["ANTHROPIC_API_KEY","DATABASE_URL","OPENAI_API_KEY","REDIS_URL"]]` — zero `STRIPE_*` of any kind; (b) `aws ssm describe-parameters --parameter-filters "Key=Name,Option=BeginsWith,Values=/luciel/"` returned six entries (`/luciel/anthropic-api-key`, `/luciel/database-url`, `/luciel/openai-api-key`, `/luciel/production/REDIS_URL`, `/luciel/production/platform-admin-key`, `/luciel/production/worker_database_url`) — zero Stripe params anywhere in the `/luciel/` namespace. The Step 30a closure stanza in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 (preserved verbatim under the doc-truthing pass on 2026-05-14 at commit `200d8e0`) describes a live customer journey through Stripe-hosted Checkout, magic-link onboarding, and Customer Portal flows — none of which has ever been reachable from prod because `settings.stripe_secret_key` has always resolved to the empty-string default at runtime. The Step 30a closure evidence on 2026-05-13 was code-level (the 46 contract tests in `app/tests/api/test_step30a_billing_shape.py`, the local-dev e2e harness `tests/e2e/step_30a_live_e2e.py` driven by a `.env` file with test-mode Stripe keys), not prod-runtime-level (no live HTTPS request against the prod ALB has ever reached Stripe). The Step 30a.2 closure stanza inherits the same caveat — the `:45` image boots clean and the migrations apply, but the new `intro_fee` Price + first-time gate + Option A line-item assembly all depend on prod credentials that have never existed.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row ("a new individual customer can find Luciel on our website, sign up, pay through Stripe Checkout, land on a magic-link confirm page, and reach a working dashboard") and CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row ("A first-time customer pays a $100 CAD intro fee at signup and gets 90 days before the recurring price kicks in") jointly require the prod backend to hold valid live-mode Stripe credentials (`STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` for outbound API calls, `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET` for inbound signature verification) plus seven `STRIPE_PRICE_*` env vars resolving to populated SSM SecureString params. The pre-30a.2 prod state satisfies none of those — the backend container reads `ANTHROPIC_API_KEY`, `DATABASE_URL`, `OPENAI_API_KEY`, `REDIS_URL` and nothing else from secrets; the Stripe-facing config keys in `app/core/config.py:176-200` all default to the empty string and there is no SSM-to-env wiring in `td-backend-rev39.json` or its successors (`:44`, `:45`) that surfaces them.
**Repo state at the time of raise:** `app/core/config.py` declares ten `stripe_*` settings (lines 176–200) with empty-string defaults. `app/integrations/stripe/client.py:232-233` reads `settings.stripe_secret_key` and `settings.stripe_webhook_secret` at client construction. `app/services/billing_service.py::resolve_price_id` reads `settings.stripe_price_*` lazily per-checkout (the laziness is what kept the container booting clean despite the missing credentials — the failure mode is a 501 on `/billing/checkout`, not a boot crash). The backend `:39` / `:44` / `:45` task-defs were registered without `STRIPE_*` secrets entries. The Step 30a-and-31-2 deploy runbook (`docs/runbooks/step-30a-and-31-2-prod-deploy.md`) names `STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET` once (line 370, in a webhook-failure recovery note) but never enumerates the SSM-puts-and-task-def-patch path for the underlying credential set. The Step 30a-1 deploy runbook prescribes SSM paths under `/luciel/prod/stripe_*` — a third path convention not used elsewhere in the actual `/luciel/` namespace (existing entries use either `/luciel/<service>-<param>` flat or `/luciel/production/<PARAM>` nested). The runbook's prescribed convention is therefore also a documentation drift against the live SSM store; this drift's resolution path adopts `/luciel/production/stripe_*` to match the existing convention and supersedes the runbook's `/luciel/prod/` prefix.
**Operational impact at the time of raise:** Zero customer impact today — no live customer exists to be affected, and the pre-30a.2 `/billing/checkout` endpoint has returned 501 since Step 30a's deploy on 2026-05-08 (the design claim of "code-complete on prod" has always been runtime-deferred, only the deferral wasn't fully named in the ledger). The discovery this session converts an ambient "how does prod actually look" question into a named drift with a closure path. Closing this drift is a strict prerequisite for closing `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13`; the activation drift is now downstream of the credentials-wiring drift, where it was previously assumed to subsume it.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30a.2 (the discovery surfaced during its GATE 3 walkthrough; the closure path lands in the same Step 30a.2 deploy sequence and the Step 30a.2 closing tag re-cut covers it). The Step 30a row in §12 also receives an annotation in the same doc-truthing commit clarifying that its 2026-05-13 closure was code-complete-not-prod-runtime; the closure stanza body stays preserved per Pass 9 doctrine (no §3 deletions).
**Resolution path:** Pattern E sequence executed in this same session. (a) **Doc-truthing first** (this commit): drift entry opens here; CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row receives an annotation clarifying that the 2026-05-13 closure was code-complete-not-prod-runtime; CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row receives an annotation clarifying that the 2026-05-14 "Code-complete on prod" status names code + schema + image, not credentials; `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` receives a 2026-05-14 annotation explicitly subsuming this drift into its closure path (single closure event, two drifts close together). (b) **SSM puts** (post-commit): nine `aws ssm put-parameter --type SecureString --overwrite --region ca-central-1` calls writing `/luciel/production/stripe_secret_key`, `/luciel/production/stripe_webhook_secret` (deferred to post-endpoint-registration sub-step), `/luciel/production/stripe_price_individual`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_individual_annual`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_team_monthly`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_team_annual`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_company_monthly`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_company_annual`, `/luciel/production/stripe_price_intro_fee`. The seven Price IDs come from `scripts/stripe_create_live_prices.py` (committed under this same step) which reads `STRIPE_SECRET_KEY` from the SSM `secret_key` param put in the same sequence and creates seven live-mode Prices via the Stripe API. (c) **Backend task-def patch**: register `luciel-backend:46` cloning `:45` with nine new `secrets` entries mapping each `STRIPE_*` env var name to the matching SSM ARN under `arn:aws:ssm:ca-central-1:729005488042:parameter/luciel/production/stripe_*`. The worker task-def receives zero Stripe secrets (confirmed by `grep -rn "import stripe" app/tasks/` returning empty — retention purges talk to Postgres only). (d) **ECS service force-redeploy** on `luciel-backend-service` so the running task reads the new task-def revision and the new secrets at start. (e) **Webhook endpoint registration**: register a live-mode webhook endpoint pointing at `https://<prod-alb-url>/api/v1/billing/webhook`, capture the `whsec_…` signing secret, SSM-put it as `/luciel/production/stripe_webhook_secret`, register `luciel-backend:47` with the webhook secret wired, force-redeploy. (f) **GATE 4 smoke**: the four-flow harness named in `D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14`'s resolution path (one first-time per tier + one cancel-rejoin per tier) plus the cascade-10-layer test under `D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14`'s resolution path. (g) **GATE 5 closing tag** re-cut `step-30a-2-trial-and-purge-complete` against the doc-truthing commit that closes this drift and `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` together.
**Pattern E:** No row mutation, no destructive operation. Nine additive SSM SecureString puts (zero existing Stripe params to overwrite); one additive task-def revision (`:46` cloned from `:45` with nine new `secrets` entries appended, no existing entries removed or changed); one additive task-def revision (`:47` cloned from `:46` with the tenth `secrets` entry for the webhook secret); two service force-redeploys (the standard ECS rolling-deploy shape, no service definition changes). The Step 30a code path is preserved untouched — `BillingService.resolve_price_id` still validates lazily per-checkout, the magic-link auth still runs, the widget surface is unaffected. The drift closes by the credentials becoming available at runtime, not by any code change.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a row (the customer-facing surface this drift names as runtime-incomplete); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row (the closing step — the credentials wiring lands here, the GATE 5 closing tag covers both this drift and the upstream activation drift); CANONICAL_RECAP §14 (Monetization — the seven-Price commitment this drift's resolution path operationalises); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — the call-site map that depends on these credentials being present); `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` (the parent drift this surfaces — its resolution path is the SSM-puts + force-redeploy half of this drift's resolution path; both close together in the Step 30a.2 closing-tag commit); `D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14` (sibling drift, design partner — the four-flow smoke this drift's GATE 4 runs is defined by that drift); `D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14` (sibling drift, design partner — the cascade-10-layer test this drift's GATE 4 runs is defined by that drift); `D-retention-purge-worker-missing-2026-05-09` (sibling drift, design partner — closed in `200d8e0`, the worker is the deferred-not-rejected pair of this drift's task-def patch); `docs/runbooks/step-30a-1-prod-deploy.md` (the runbook whose `/luciel/prod/stripe_*` path-convention prescription this drift supersedes with `/luciel/production/stripe_*`).
