Drift will be expanded with the description, then we decide whether the cause is a design gap (e.g., visibility timeout vs job duration), a code bug (idempotency or ack handling), or an operational incident (poison messages stuck redelivering).

### D-step-24-5c-and-31-schema-and-code-undeployed-to-prod-2026-05-12

**Status:** OPEN — active risk window; blocks any code deploy from `main` until closed.
**Raised by:** Partner (Aryan) on 2026-05-12 during Step 31 close-out review, after correctly challenging the agent's incorrect framing that "no prod deploy was needed." The agent had assessed Step 31's PRs in isolation without walking the Alembic migration graph forward from the last known production-deployed revision — a sloppy review that this entry exists to correct.
**Design claim:** Two ARCHITECTURE sections describe a feature surface that, on the current `main` HEAD `fa876ce`, has live application code but no live database schema on production RDS: §3.2.11 (Identity & conversation continuity — Step 24.5c) and §3.2.12 (Hierarchical dashboards & validation gate — Step 31). Both subsections are marked ✅ Implemented and the corresponding CANONICAL_RECAP rows are marked ✅. The implementation claim is correct at the code-and-local-Postgres level; the production-deployment claim is **not asserted by either row today, but the absence of a `[PROD-PHASE-2B]` marker or a Prod observed-clean stanza is itself misleading without this entry** — a reader could reasonably infer the surfaces are live in production, and they are not.
**Repo state:**
  - **Alembic head on `main`:** `3dbbc70d0105` (`alembic/versions/3dbbc70d0105_step24_5c_conversations_and_identity_claims.py`) introduces the `conversations` table, the `identity_claim_type` Postgres enum, the `identity_claims` table (with composite uniqueness on `(claim_type, claim_value, tenant_id, domain_id)` and two partial indexes filtered on `active=true`), and the nullable `conversation_id` FK column on `sessions`. The migration chain prior to head is `a7c1f4e92b85` (Step 30b widget columns on `api_keys`) → `d8e2c4b1a0f3` (Step 29.y Cluster 4 worker rejection-audit idempotency index) → `c5d8a1e7b3f9` (Step 29.y Cluster 3 `admin_audit_logs.row_hash NOT NULL`).
  - **Last production-deployed revision (inferred from the Step 30c prod observed-clean stanza):** ECR digest `sha256:f0bf303272fb0801eefc4cf0d20d2ddb624f2a5f60c8e845cbe422869739f863` built from `main` HEAD `84339a3`, registered as `luciel-backend:39` and `luciel-worker:19` on 2026-05-11. That image predates merge `1e761a6` (Step 24.5c sub-branch 1 — the only commit since Step 30c that touches `alembic/versions/`), so production RDS is presumed to be at `a7c1f4e92b85` (one revision behind head); production application code is presumed to be at `84339a3` (does not contain Step 24.5c models, `CrossSessionRetriever`, `IdentityResolver`, adapter claims wiring, the Step 31 widget audit log emissions, the `create_session_with_identity` route wiring in `app/api/v1/chat_widget.py`, the `DashboardService`, or the `app/api/v1/dashboard.py` HTTP surface). "Presumed" is the correct word — closing this drift includes running `alembic current` against production RDS to confirm the actual revision before the deploy.
  - **Why the gap is currently latent, not active:** production code and production schema are *both* older than the missing pieces and are internally consistent at the older state. The widget chat path on production today calls into the pre-Step-24.5c code path that does not touch `identity_claims` or `conversations`. The first deploy of any code from current `main` to production breaks this consistency: new code will execute `SessionService.create_session_with_identity()` on every widget turn (PR #30 wired it into the route), which inserts into `identity_claims` and `conversations` — tables that do not exist on production RDS — and the widget chat surface will start returning errors on every call. This is the exact failure mode the harness caught locally on 2026-05-12 before the local `alembic upgrade head` (`psycopg.errors.UndefinedTable: relation "identity_claims" does not exist`).
**Operational impact:** Zero today; high tomorrow if any code deploy is taken from `main` without first running the Alembic migration on production RDS. The risk surface is the widget chat path — i.e., the surface customers actually exercise. This entry exists specifically so no future deploy can happen without seeing this warning first.
**Owning roadmap step:** None today — this is a deploy gap, not a design or implementation gap. The work to close it is a prod-deploy event in the Step 30c precedent shape (runbook + ordered execution + observed-clean stanza), executed as a stand-alone piece of scope. It does not earn a new roadmap row because the implementation work for both Step 24.5c and Step 31 is complete on `main`; what remains is operational delivery of work already shipped.
**Resolution path (canonical ordering):**
  1. **Pre-deploy verification:** `alembic current` against production RDS to confirm the actual head revision matches the inferred `a7c1f4e92b85`. If it does not, the runbook plan is revised before any forward migration is run.
  2. **Schema first:** run `alembic upgrade head` against production RDS to advance from `a7c1f4e92b85` to `3dbbc70d0105`. This is additive only (one enum, two tables, one nullable FK column, two partial indexes) — no destructive operations, no column type changes, no NOT NULL backfills required on existing rows. Existing `sessions` rows keep `conversation_id IS NULL` which is the Step 24.5c design contract per ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11. Run inside a transaction (Alembic default for PostgreSQL); if any step fails the partial state is rolled back.
  3. **Code second:** build ECR image from `main` HEAD `fa876ce`, push under a Step-24.5c/31-naming ECR tag, register new `luciel-backend` and `luciel-worker` task-definition revisions (likely `:40` and `:20`, succeeding `:39` and `:19`), update the in-repo manifests in the same doc-truthing commit (`td-backend-rev39.json` → `td-backend-rev40.json`, `td-worker-rev19.json` → `td-worker-rev20.json`) per the precedent set by Step 30c.
  4. **Observed-clean verification:** post-deploy log review of `/ecs/luciel-backend` and `/ecs/luciel-worker` for the canonical clean-startup sequence (`Started server process [1]` → `Application startup complete.` → steady `GET /health → 200 OK`; worker `celery@... ready.` and old-worker `Warm shutdown`); zero `ERROR` / `Traceback` / `CRITICAL` hits across the post-deploy log window; deploymentCircuitBreaker did not fire on either service. Then exercise the widget chat path against the production embed key from the Stage 1 staging E2E (`luc_sk_xwij1...`, id 698, on `domain_configs.id=374`) for one end-to-end turn through `POST /api/v1/chat/widget`, watching for the three new audit log lines (`widget_chat_turn_received`, `widget_chat_session_resolved`, `widget_chat_turn_completed`) in `/ecs/luciel-backend` and the expected three new row writes (`identity_claims`, `conversations`, `sessions` with `conversation_id` populated) via a scoped read query.
  5. **Doc-truthing close:** add a **Prod observed-clean** stanza to both CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 24.5c and Step 31 rows in the Step 30c precedent shape (ECR digest, task-definition revisions, log evidence, runbook of record), append a CLOSED note to this drift entry, move this entry from §3 to §5 with strikethrough heading per §6 doctrine, and re-cut the closing tags `step-24-5c-cross-channel-identity-complete` and `step-31-dashboards-validation-gate-complete` forward onto the doc-truthing commit so the tags continue to read "code + docs + prod all agree here." Runbook of record will live at `docs/runbooks/step-24-5c-and-31-prod-deploy.md`.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** This entry is the first half of closing the honesty gap. The second half is two parenthetical notes appended in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 — one on the Step 24.5c row, one on the Step 31 row — pointing readers to this drift. The ✅ markers stay (the implementation is implemented), but the parentheticals make the deploy gap unmissable. ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 and §3.2.12 do not need a marker change because they describe design state, which is correct; the gap is operational.

Prod ECS task-definition revisions advance from `luciel-backend:39` + `luciel-worker:19` to a new revision pair (likely `:40` + `:20`) carrying the combined Step 24.5c + Step 30a + Step 31.2 code surface. ## Section 5 — Resolved drifts (kept for audit)

Closed drifts are kept here permanently with a strikethrough heading. The closing commit, the closing tag (if applicable), and a one-line resolution note are recorded. This makes the audit chain of design decisions walkable backwards; nothing is rewritten or deleted.

### ~~D-magic-link-only-auth-no-password-fallback-2026-05-16~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-16.
**Closing tag (cut and pushed):** `step-30a-3-password-auth-magic-link-fallback-complete` on doc-truthing commit `9ade0ea` (`aryanonline/Luciel:main`).
**Closing commits, in order (Luciel backend repo unless noted):** `71bd3b9` (doc-truth pre-build: password mandatory at signup across all three tiers locked into CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.3 row + ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 Auth model) → `3c89a71` (C1–C4: Alembic `a3c1f08b9d42` adds `users.password_hash VARCHAR(255) NULL` chained on `dfea1a04e037`; `AuthService` exposes argon2id `verify_password` / `set_password` / `request_password_reset` with constant-time sentinel-hash fallback and 8-char floor; `MagicLinkService` adds `mint_set_password_token(purpose=signup|invite)` + `mint_reset_password_token` + paired `consume_*` with distinct `typ` claims blocking cross-class replay; `EmailService` adds `send_welcome_set_password_email` with stable `[welcome-set-password-email]` log marker; `/api/v1/auth` router registers the three documented POST routes; `billing_webhook_service._on_checkout_completed` swaps the post-checkout magic-link email for the welcome-set-password email **in place of**, not in addition to, the prior mint) → `d55105c` (C5: `tests/api/test_step30a_3_auth_shape.py` 27/27 green; `app/middleware/auth.py` `SKIP_AUTH_PATHS` includes `/api/v1/auth`) → `f89dac2` (C6: doc-truth Option B welcome-email mechanic into DRIFTS + ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13) → `8b83b5e` (C4 follow-up: `/onboarding/claim` rewired off the magic-link path) → `13b431e` on `aryanonline/Luciel-Website` (C7: `src/lib/auth.ts`, `src/pages/Login.tsx` rewrite, `src/pages/ForgotPassword.tsx`, `src/pages/SetPassword.tsx`, `src/components/Nav.tsx` "Log in" link, `src/App.tsx` route registration, `src/lib/analytics.ts` event types extended) → `5b75dc9` → `949b05f` → `cf1ba2c` → `cfe51fd` (C8 deploy arc: image `sha256:ca8f24e8bd3c127b2808585ce3d4f6ab4ab9c2e8eec6e582954e954e65ac73a2` pushed to ECR `729005488042.dkr.ecr.ca-central-1.amazonaws.com/luciel-backend`; task-def `luciel-backend:64` registered + service rolled PRIMARY 1/1 desired=1 running=1; Alembic upgrade `dfea1a04e037 -> a3c1f08b9d42` ran in container init and `alembic current` verified `a3c1f08b9d42 (head)` via ECS exec) → this doc-truthing commit.
**Resolution:** Password authentication is now the daily-login primitive across all three tiers (Individual $100, Team $300, Company $1,000); magic-link is retired as a daily-login primitive and survives only as the bootstrap and recovery primitive. Password is mandatory at signup — not opt-in — gated by the Option B welcome-email mechanic that issues the set-password link **after** `checkout.session.completed` commits the `User` row, eliminating the Stripe-Checkout → webhook race window that Option A URL-exchange would have surfaced. The Stripe Checkout success page (`/onboarding`) is passive ("Check your email") and grants no cookied `/app` session; the buyer must redeem the welcome email's `/auth/set-password?token=…` link, set a ≥8-char password, and auto-route to `/dashboard`. The cookie shape and Step 31.2 middleware contract are unchanged. **Live E2E proof (2026-05-16 ≈21:06 EDT, captured this commit):** Aryan completed a real $100 paid Individual signup in incognito on `vantagemind.ai` end-to-end — Pricing → Stripe Checkout → `/onboarding` landing → welcome-set-password email delivered → `/auth/set-password?token=…` accepted password → auto-route to `/dashboard` → sign-out → `/login` with email+password → back on `/dashboard`. All four gates green on the prod surface. **Smoke probe proof:** `POST https://api.vantagemind.ai/api/v1/auth/forgot-password` with valid-TLD payload returns `HTTP/1.1 200` with neutral body `{"ok":true,"message":"If an account exists, a reset link has been sent."}` — confirms the route is mounted, the `SKIP_AUTH_PATHS` exemption works, argon2id + JWT init did not crash the container, and the no-enumeration contract holds. **Smoke deploy lesson (closed in `cfe51fd`):** Pydantic `EmailStr` (`email-validator`) rejects reserved TLDs per RFC 2606 (`.invalid`, `.test`, `.example`, `.localhost`); both deploy scripts (`scripts/deploy_30a3.ps1`, `scripts/deploy_30a3_rollforward.ps1`) now use a real-domain smoke email (response is neutral 200 either way, so this does not hit a real inbox).
**Pattern E:** Additive end-to-end — new column (nullable), new service surface, new routes, new pages. The existing magic-link flow is unchanged structurally; only the post-checkout `_on_checkout_completed` mint path was retargeted from magic-link to welcome-set-password (the helper itself remains for forgot-password use). The cookie shape is identical, so Step 31.2's middleware contract holds without modification. No row mutation on pre-existing data: existing users carry `password_hash IS NULL` until they next pass through the forgot-password recovery surface.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.3 row (the design home this drift closes against); CANONICAL_RECAP §13.1 T1 / T5 (the acceptance scenarios this closure underwrites for the Team and Company tiers — invite-acceptance is the first password-set event using the same `/auth/set-password` route with `purpose=invite`); ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 “Auth model” (the implementation home — Option B welcome-email mechanic locked there); `D-magic-link-auth-cookie-session-2026-05-13` (the predecessor drift on cookie session shape — stays OPEN through Step 32a's broader auth story; this closure carves out the password-fallback + mandatory-at-signup slice only); `D-team-self-serve-incomplete-invite-ui-missing-2026-05-16` and `D-company-self-serve-incomplete-org-building-ui-missing-2026-05-16` (strict dependents this closure unblocks — both invite flows now re-use the `/auth/set-password` route with `purpose=invite`); `D-deploy-script-jq-filter-container-name-mismatch-2026-05-16` (sibling deploy-toolchain drift — `cf1ba2c` hardened the C8 script against the container-rename failure mode by dynamically verifying `ContainerName="luciel-backend"` and asserting pre/post-rewrite image swap; the sibling drift's broader fix on every `scripts/deploy_*.sh` remains OPEN).

### ~~D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14
**Closing tag (planned):** `step-30a-2-trial-and-purge-complete` on the doc-truthing commit that follows the Stripe-activation operational close.
**Closing commits, in order:** `3afc866` (step 30a.2 — paid-intro trial + retention worker + cascade extension; Alembic migration adding `deactivated_at` on `conversations`, `identity_claims`, `messages` with partial index on `(tenant_id) WHERE deactivated_at IS NULL`; `AdminService.deactivate_tenant_with_cascade` extended to flip the three new layers leaf-first within the same transaction) → this doc-truthing commit (recording the closure across the three docs).
**Resolution:** The cascade now flips ten of ten scope-bearing layers under a deactivated tenant in one transaction — the pre-30a.2 seven (`domain_configs`, `agent_configs`, `luciel_instances`, `api_keys`, `memories`, `sessions`, `scope_assignments`) plus the new three (`conversations`, `identity_claims`, `messages`). `messages` is scoped via the `session_id` FK chain rather than its own `tenant_id` column. Leaf-first delete order is preserved so the FK ON DELETE RESTRICT contracts on `conversations.tenant_id` and `identity_claims.tenant_id` cannot block the eventual hard-delete the retention worker performs after the 90-day window.
**Pattern E:** Three additive columns + one additive index; no destructive operations; existing rows backfill as `deactivated_at IS NULL` (active state). No row mutation on pre-existing data — the cascade extension writes timestamps it never wrote before, and pre-existing soft-deleted rows are not retroactively touched.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — "Pattern E on cancel"), ARCHITECTURE §4.4 (Soft-delete by default — retention-worker bullet flipped 📋 → ✅ in this same commit), ARCHITECTURE §4.5 (Cascade-correct departure — the symmetry contract this drift closed against), CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row, CANONICAL_RECAP T11 (the customer-observable contract), `~~D-retention-purge-worker-missing-2026-05-09~~` (sibling closure in the same commit), `~~D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14~~` (sibling Step 30a.2 closure — the trial-policy half of the same step).

### ~~D-trial-policy-mixed-per-tier-2026-05-14~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14 (code-side closure; Stripe-side operational close follows at GATE 3 — see `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` §3 annotation)
**Closing tag (planned):** `step-30a-2-trial-and-purge-complete` on the doc-truthing commit that follows the Stripe-activation operational close.
**Closing commits, in order:** `3afc866` (step 30a.2 — `billing_service.py` `TRIAL_DAYS` map replaced with `INTRO_TRIAL_DAYS = 90` constant + `intro_fee_price_id` resolution + `is_first_time_customer(email)` gate via `func.lower(User.email)` + Stripe Option A line-item assembly for first-time signups; `app/core/config.py` adds `stripe_price_intro_fee` setting; new `tests/api/test_first_time_gate.py` + updated `tests/api/test_step30a_1_tiered_self_serve_shape.py`) → this doc-truthing commit.
**Resolution:** Trial policy is uniform across all six (tier, cadence) primitives: $100 CAD one-time intro + 90-day trial on the recurring price, gated to first-time-ever customers by case-insensitive email lookup against the historical customers table. Cancel + rejoin = standard plan rate with no second intro (Pattern E for customer history: the `is_first_time_customer` predicate is a read against persisted customer rows, never a write). The seven-Price Stripe design (six recurring + one intro_fee) is locked in code; the seven live Prices + seven SSM puts land at GATE 3 when Stripe activation completes.
**Pattern E:** Internal-only application-state replacement (no audit-row footprint, no live customer rows touched). The `is_first_time_customer` gate reads existing customer rows; it does not write to them. The pre-30a.2 `TRIAL_DAYS` constant is replaced because the audit chain begins at the Stripe webhook event, not at the trial-policy decision.
**Cross-refs:** CANONICAL_RECAP §14 (Monetization — intro-offer bullet added in this same commit), CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row, ARCHITECTURE §3.2.13 (Billing surface — extended in this same commit with the intro_fee + 90d trial mechanics), `D-stripe-live-account-not-yet-activated-2026-05-13` (upstream operational gate — the seven-Price design lands in code first, then the Stripe activation form lands the seven live Prices), `~~D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14~~` (sibling Step 30a.2 closure — the cascade half of the same step).

### ~~D-retention-purge-worker-missing-2026-05-09~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-14 by Step 30a.2
**Closing tag (planned):** `step-30a-2-trial-and-purge-complete` on the doc-truthing commit that follows the Stripe-activation operational close.
**Closing commits:** `3afc866` (step 30a.2 — `app/worker/tasks/retention.py::run_retention_purge` Celery task; `AdminService.hard_delete_tenant_after_retention` method walks `deactivated_at < now() - 90 days` and hard-deletes leaf-first; `app/worker/celery_app.py` beat schedule `retention-purge-nightly` at `crontab(hour=8, minute=0)` UTC; `Dockerfile.worker` injects `--beat` so the embedded beat scheduler enqueues the nightly tick) → this doc-truthing commit.
**Resolution:** The scheduled retention purge worker exists. The policy in `app/policy/retention.py` is now enforced by a 08:00 UTC nightly Celery beat schedule that walks tenants with `deactivated_at < now() - INTERVAL '90 days'` and hard-deletes them leaf-first through the cascade-complete soft-delete graph that `~~D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14~~` closed in this same commit. The retention worker is therefore load-bearing on the cascade extension; the two drifts closed as a single Step 30a.2 deliverable, in the order (cascade first, then the worker that depends on it). The 90-day window matches the contracted retention period named in CANONICAL_RECAP T11; §4.4's storage-cost story is now defended by the worker the architecture claimed existed. AdminAuditLog rows survive the purge per the audit-chain integrity contract in §3.4. New open drift `D-celery-beat-single-replica-coupling-2026-05-14` records the embedded-beat single-replica constraint as known future-debt.
**Pattern E:** The retention worker is additive (a new Celery task + a new beat schedule entry + a `--beat` flag on the worker container). Hard-delete on tenants past the retention window is the explicit §4.4 exception to soft-delete-by-default — the design always commit to this; the implementation finally honours it. AdminAuditLog rows are intentionally preserved across the hard-delete because the audit chain must remain walkable after a tenant departs the platform.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.4 (Background worker tier — retention-purge bullet flipped 📋 → ✅ in this same commit; Triangulation line retargeted from Step 34 to Step 30a.2), ARCHITECTURE §4.4 (Soft-delete by default — retention-worker bullet flipped 📋 → ✅ in this same commit), ARCHITECTURE §3.4 (audit-chain integrity contract — AdminAuditLog survives the purge), CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30a.2 row, CANONICAL_RECAP T11 (the customer-observable contract), `~~D-cancellation-cascade-incomplete-conversations-claims-2026-05-14~~` (sibling closure — the cascade-completion prerequisite the worker depends on), `D-celery-beat-single-replica-coupling-2026-05-14` (new OPEN future-debt drift opened in this same commit recording the embedded-beat constraint), `D-celery-worker-runs-as-root-2026-05-11` (sibling worker-tier hygiene drift — different gap, same subsection).

SSM write is rejected for embed keys at the service layer because the customer cannot read SSM. ### ~~D-ci-ast-job-red-on-main-2026-05-08~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-10 (this commit on `step-30b-cleanup`)
**Closing commit:** `9e9cb9e` (this branch's commit (b): `.github/workflows/ci.yml` step "run http_client params + health pytest tests" gains a step-scoped `env: DATABASE_URL: "sqlite:///:memory:"`)
**Closing verification:** Next CI run on the merge of `step-30b-cleanup` into `main` must show the AST job green.
**Raised by:** Discovery on 2026-05-10 while watching the first widget-cdn-deploy run end-to-end. The `gh run list --branch main` history showed the `ast-and-unit-tests` job had been silently red on every push to `main` for at least nine consecutive merges (2026-05-08 `5f297b73` through 2026-05-10 `85990c4`), in every case interrupted by the same collection error: `tests/api/test_health.py` imports `app.main`, which transitively imports `app.core.config` and instantiates `settings = Settings()` at module-load time; `Settings.database_url: str` has no default, so a CI runner with no `DATABASE_URL` exported fails the Pydantic field validator before any test runs.
**Why it persisted unseen:** The CI gate landed in Step 29 D (`89afbae`) at the same time `tests/api/test_health.py` was added. Both pieces work locally because development environments export `DATABASE_URL` from `.env`. The first push to `main` after Step 29 D was the first run with a bare-runner environment, and the failure was already in place. Subsequent merges all failed for the same reason and no one watched the run output. This is the doctrine "red signals stop being signals when ignored" failure mode — visible only because the widget-cdn-deploy run brought the Actions tab back under daily attention.
**Resolution:** `tests/api/test_health.py` calls `/health`, which returns `{"status": "ok", "service": settings.app_name}` and does not touch the DB. So the CI fix is to provide the minimum literal value that lets `Settings()` validate and `create_engine()` resolve a dialect: `sqlite:///:memory:`. SQLite ships with SQLAlchemy core; no install-set change is required. The `env:` block is scoped to the one step that needs it, so the next step (pillar harness collection) keeps its no-DATABASE_URL skip-cleanly contract.
**What is deliberately NOT done:** `Settings.database_url` is still required-with-no-default. Loosening that field would make the model tolerate a misconfigured production runtime, which is the wrong tradeoff. The CI shim is the right place for the workaround, not the model. A future refactor that wants AST-only static-analysis CI would lazy-instantiate `settings` or split `BootSettings` from `RuntimeSettings`; that's a Step-29 verification-doctrine question, out of scope here.
**Pattern E:** No application behavior changed. The production runtime path is untouched. This is a workflow-file-only edit adding a step-scoped env var.
**Pass 9 doctrine note (2026-05-13):** This entry was born §5-only post-doctrine (closure commit `8ad59e4` on 2026-05-10 added the §5 strikethrough heading without ever introducing a §3 entry; the parent of `8ad59e4` also lacked a §3 body). Pass 9 leaves the entry as-is because (a) the §5 entry is rich enough to carry the design-claim and repo-state context that a §3 entry would have held, and (b) reconstructing a §3 body now would be invention rather than restoration. Honesty cataloged here; no restoration possible. Tracked in `D-pass-6-mirror-restoration-incomplete-three-deletions-missed-2026-05-13` for completeness.

### ~~D-widget-no-content-safety-or-scope-guardrail-2026-05-10~~

**Status:** OPEN — load-bearing for customer trust; tracked against roadmap Step 30d
**Raised by:** Step 30b Phase 4 staging E2E. With domain_config 374 (`tenant=luciel-staging-widget-test`, `domain=cloudfront-staging`, `system_prompt_additions=NULL`) bound to embed key 698, the live widget at `https://d1t84i96t71fsi.cloudfront.net/staging-widget-test.html` accepted and answered an off-topic request ("how are you doing") and engaged substantively with a sensitive-content request ("I need help making a sex toy"). The widget is generally helpful; it is not customer-deployable.
**Design claim:** CANONICAL_RECAP §4 commits Luciel to a behavior contract — staying in scope of what the customer site is for, declining requests outside that scope politely, and refusing sensitive-content engagement that would damage the customer's reputation. ARCHITECTURE §3.3 step 8 (action classification) covers tool-call gating but says nothing about message-content gating. Neither doc currently commits to a content-safety layer or a per-domain on-topic guardrail.
**Repo state:** No content-safety check exists in the request path. `app/policy/` has no moderation module. The chat service threads `domain_config.system_prompt_additions` into the system prompt — that column is the only existing knob — but the staging row was created with `NULL` and the issuance path does not require it to be non-null before a widget goes live. No provider-side moderation API call (OpenAI moderation, Anthropic content filters) is wired into the chat pipeline. The only existing constraint that touches content is `EMBED_REQUIRED_PERMISSIONS = frozenset(['chat'])`, which gates surfaces (no tool calls from widget) but not the content of conversational turns.
**Two distinct gaps inside this drift:**
  - **Gap A — on-topic scoping.** Per-domain prompt that constrains the widget to the customer's vertical. Mitigation today is operational (write `system_prompt_additions` correctly before going live). Real fix is a (1) preflight validator that refuses to mint an embed key against a domain with NULL or empty `system_prompt_additions`, (2) a template library of vetted scope prompts (real estate, support, sales) operators can pick from, and (3) a CI test that asserts an out-of-scope question receives a decline-with-redirect.
  - **Gap B — content safety.** Sensitive/adult/illegal-content refusal, independent of vertical. Cannot be done with prompt alone — needs a moderation gate (provider API or in-process classifier) before the LLM call, and a sanitized refusal response that does not leak the offending text into traces.
**Owning roadmap step:** Step 30d (Widget content safety and scope guardrails) — adopted into CANONICAL_RECAP §12 on 2026-05-10 (commit `d2b05c46`), sitting between Step 30c (action classification — tool gating) and Step 31 (dashboards + validation gate). Step 30c gates *what Luciel does*; Step 30d gates *what Luciel says and what it engages with*. They are sibling problems, not parent/child, and folding 30d into 30c would dilute both. Step 30d's success criterion: with a real REMAX-style domain config, the widget (1) declines an off-topic question with a graceful redirect to the customer's vertical and (2) refuses sensitive-content engagement with a fixed, sanitized response that never reaches the LLM provider's traces in raw form. This drift closes when Step 30d closes.
**Immediate mitigation (Step 30b tail, not Step 30d):** Populate `domain_configs.id=374` with a real-estate scoping and refusal prompt via `PATCH /api/v1/admin/domains/luciel-staging-widget-test/cloudfront-staging` so the staging widget refuses both the off-topic test and the sex-toy test. This raises the floor for the REMAX demo without closing the drift. The drift stays OPEN until Step 30d's preflight validator, provider-side moderation gate, and CI tests land.
**Doc-truthing this pass:** CANONICAL_RECAP §12 carries the Step 30d row (committed `d2b05c46`) that explicitly names this drift as one of its two closing conditions. No ARCHITECTURE prose change yet — Step 30d's design-shape edits (moderation gate in §3.3 and issuance-time preflight in §3.2.2) land surgically when the build lands, per DRIFTS §6 doctrine that a new roadmap step on its own is not a reason to grow the design docs.
**Closeout 2026-05-11 — RESOLVED on full closure (both Gap A on-topic scoping AND Gap B content safety addressed):**
**Closing tag (planned):** `step-30d-content-safety-complete` on merge of `step-30d` into `main`.
**Closing PRs, in order:** #14 (Deliverable A: issuance-time scope-prompt preflight, merged `3cbd489`) → #15 (Deliverable B: per-turn provider-agnostic content-safety moderation gate, fail-closed, default OpenAI, `KeywordModerationProvider` added in 30d-C for deterministic E2E refusal-path coverage, merged `c7d958e`) → #16 (Deliverable C: widget-surface E2E CI harness behind `workflow_dispatch` in v1 + AST contract test, merged `146f133`).
**Resolution:** Gap A closed by the preflight validator (`app/services/scope_prompt_preflight.py`) that refuses to mint a domain-scoped embed key unless the bound `domain_configs.system_prompt_additions` is non-empty; tenant-wide mints intentionally skip the preflight and surface a non-fatal warning, since they pre-date a domain selection. Gap B closed by the per-turn moderation gate in `app/policy/moderation.py` wired into `POST /api/v1/chat/widget`, fail-closed, sanitized SSE refusal (HTTP 200, same three-frame contract so the gate is not fingerprintable), categories never returned to the client. Step 30d Deliverable C adds the harness that exercises both gates against a real backend; in v1 it runs `workflow_dispatch`-only and the AST shape contract is pinned in the backend-free CI lane via `tests/api/test_widget_e2e_harness_shape.py`.
**Pattern E note:** The planned follow-up that adds `pull_request` alongside `workflow_dispatch` in `widget-e2e.yml` keeps the v1 trigger untouched per Pattern E (never delete — deactivate by replacement). The AST contract test's `pull_request absent in v1` assertion is documented in `ci/e2e/README.md` and will flip atomically with that follow-up commit.
**First clean harness run:** widget-e2e dispatch `25695322187` on `main` (2026-05-11, 1m21s, every assertion green end-to-end: alembic upgrades through `b0e003ffa07f`, uvicorn ready on `/health` attempt 3, four admin endpoints 200, happy-path SSE three-frame contract via stub LLM provider, refusal-path REFUSAL_MESSAGE frame via KeywordModerationProvider sentinel) is the observed-clean evidence that flipped CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30d row 🔧 → ✅ in commit `21d7101`. Three pre-existing harness gaps surfaced between the step-30d merge (`4e7ffbc`) and the first clean run and were closed by Pattern E follow-up branches against `main` (never against `step-30d`): pgvector postgres image pin (PR #18 / `ff0e116`, closed run `25690719076` CREATE EXTENSION vector failure), readiness probe path `/healthz` → `/health` (PR #19 / `b517f29`, closed run `25693123650` 404 failure), hermetic stub LLM provider with default-False settings flag + construction-time WARNING (PR #20 / `ec8a72d`, closed run `25694850046` zero-providers failure). Each follow-up extended `tests/api/test_widget_e2e_harness_shape.py` (14 → 15 → 18 tests) to pin the cross-file invariant at PR-time in the backend-free CI lane. No new drifts opened — all three were pre-existing harness inaccuracies surfaced by the first real dispatch, not Step 30d regressions. Cross-refs: ARCHITECTURE §3.2.2 *Issuance* (Gap A surface — preflight validator), §3.3 step 6.5 (Gap B surface — moderation gate), §4.9 (rejected-alternative bullet on prompt-only content gating); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 30d row carries the ✅ marker landed by this same arc.
**Pattern E follow-up landed:** PR #21 merged into `main` as squash commit `e02c282` (2026-05-11), adding `pull_request:` trigger alongside `workflow_dispatch:` in `.github/workflows/widget-e2e.yml` pinned to an 11-path widget-surface allowlist. Run `25697100429` on that PR is the first observed clean `pull_request`-triggered widget-e2e run in repo history (~1m21s, all assertions green) — the v2 trigger self-validated on its own PR once parse-valid. Implementation finding documented in commit history: GitHub Actions parser treats `paths` and `paths-ignore` as mutually exclusive for the same event (a v1 attempt with both was rejected at parse-time, 0s no-jobs failure on run `25696913391`, fixed in the same PR by dropping `paths-ignore` since `paths` already excludes non-matching PRs; sub-tree exclusions go via `!`-prefix inside `paths`). AST contract (`tests/api/test_widget_e2e_harness_shape.py`) grew 18 → 19 tests: the v1 negative `pull_request absent` assertion flipped to a v2 positive `both triggers present` assertion plus a new pin that `pull_request.paths` is the exact 11-entry widget-surface subset and `paths-ignore` is absent — matching the surgical AST-growth pattern of PRs #18/#19/#20.

### ~~D-confirmation-gate-not-enforced-2026-05-09~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-11 (build complete on `step-30c`, merged to `main`, closing tag cut, **and observed enforcing in production on the same day** — see Prod observed-clean note below).
**Closing tag:** `step-30c-action-classification-complete` on `main` commit `99c6eb5` (the doc-truthing commit where code and all three docs first agree that Step 30c is closed; the underlying code-complete commit is `b216300`, three commits earlier — the tag was deliberately re-cut forward onto the doc-truthing commit so the auditor can read the tag as "code + docs agree here"). Merge of `step-30c` into `main` on 2026-05-11.
**Raised by:** Architecture §3.3 step 8 ("Policy gate"), §4.9 (synchronous-only invocation rejected); Canonical Recap §4 (behavior contracts: "Luciel does not take consequential action without permission").
**Original design claim (kept for audit):** Tool invocations are classified into three tiers — **routine** (just do it, audited), **notify-and-proceed** (execute and surface visibly to the customer), and **approval-required** (return a confirmation request before executing). Approval is required only when an action is genuinely consequential — irreversible, high-blast-radius, off-pattern relative to the customer's established usage, or where Luciel itself is uncertain. Routine and reversible external-facing actions are not gated, because gating them would make Luciel feel timid and bureaucratic and would violate the senior-advisor voice in Recap §3.
**Resolution:** The three-tier gate is now enforced server-side at the tool broker. `app/policy/action_classification.py` ships a pluggable provider in the same shape as `app/policy/moderation.py` (Step 30d Deliverable B): `ActionTier` enum (ROUTINE / NOTIFY_AND_PROCEED / APPROVAL_REQUIRED), a Protocol-based `ActionClassifier`, a `StaticTierRegistryClassifier` that reads each tool's `declared_tier` from the class body, a `FailClosedActionClassifier` wrapper that converts `ToolTierUndeclared` *and* arbitrary exceptions into APPROVAL_REQUIRED (so an undeclared tier or a future memory-backed off-pattern detector that errors cannot silently escalate privilege), a `NullActionClassifier` for dev with a per-call WARNING, and an `ActionClassificationGate.from_settings` factory. Two new `Settings` knobs (`action_classifier='static'`, `action_classifier_fail_closed=True`) default to the production wiring; an unknown provider value raises `ConfigurationError` at boot. `LucielTool.declared_tier: ActionTier | None = None` on the base class is the new opt-in surface every concrete tool must override; an inherited `None` fails closed to APPROVAL_REQUIRED by design. The three shipped tools were tiered in the same commit: `save_memory` and `get_session_summary` ROUTINE, `escalate_to_human` NOTIFY_AND_PROCEED (the rationale for each tier is recorded in a class-body comment next to the declaration so a reviewer cannot miss it). `ToolBroker.execute_tool` now classifies before dispatch (the call-order invariant is pinned at AST level in `tests/api/test_action_classification.py`), stamps `tier` / `tier_reason` / `classifier` onto every `ToolResult.metadata` with four deliberately-distinct reason codes for audit clarity — `'declared_tier'` (normal classification), `'unknown_tool'` (the broker did not find the tool name in the registry; a stray name from the LLM), `'tier_undeclared'` (the registered tool's maintainer forgot to set `declared_tier` and the fail-closed wrapper caught the `ToolTierUndeclared` exception), and `'classifier_error'` (the classifier raised an arbitrary exception and the wrapper translated it); all three refusal codes still route to APPROVAL_REQUIRED but an auditor can tell the failure modes apart, and short-circuits APPROVAL_REQUIRED with a pending frame containing `pending=True`, `tool_name`, and `proposed_parameters` so the runtime layer can render a confirmation prompt. The historical `ToolBroker(registry)` signature is preserved per Pattern E by making the classifier parameter optional and lazy-importing `settings` for the default. Test coverage in `tests/api/test_action_classification.py` is 28 tests across AST contract + behavioural inline-fakes, mirroring the house style of `tests/api/test_content_safety_gate.py`; the suite runs in the existing backend-free CI lane and pins (a) the action-classification module's public surface, (b) the `ActionTier` enum has exactly three members, (c) `FailClosedActionClassifier.classify` catches both `ToolTierUndeclared` and `Exception`, (d) the broker constructor accepts an injectable classifier, (e) `self._classifier.classify` runs at a lower line number than `tool.execute`, (f) the APPROVAL_REQUIRED `if` branch contains a `Return` at a lower line number than `tool.execute`, (g) the three shipped tiers, (h) `LucielTool.declared_tier=None` default on the base class, and (i) end-to-end broker behaviour against a real `ToolRegistry` for all four code paths (ROUTINE executes, NOTIFY_AND_PROCEED executes, unknown-tool refuses, undeclared-tier refuses without executing). A partner-level live end-to-end harness at `tests/e2e/step_30c_live_e2e.py` (33 claims, backend-free, runs in under a second) exercises the shipped `ToolBroker` + `ToolRegistry` + shipped `LucielTool` subclasses against every English-language clause in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 row 30c — the first per-step live-e2e harness on the project, establishing a precedent documented in `tests/e2e/README.md` (one harness per closed step, a step is not "closed" until its harness is green on the closing branch). The harness caught the audit-signal collision (`tier_reason='unknown_tool'` reused for two operationally-different failure modes) before merge that the 28 unit tests missed; the surgical fix landed on the same branch as follow-up commit `becd92b`.
**Doc-truthing landed in the same commit:** `ARCHITECTURE.md` §3.3 step 8 flipped 📋 → ✅ with the implementation paragraph appended; §4.9 synchronous-only rejected-alternative bullet flipped to ✅ with a reference to the AST contract test that pins the call-order invariant; `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §4 (the "On consequential" note) and §5 step 4 (the operating loop) both flipped their 30c references from 🔧 "lands in 30c" to ✅ "landed in 30c"; §12 row for Step 30c flipped 📋 → ✅ with the full closeout detail.
**Deliberate non-goals at v1 (carried forward, not regressions):**
  - Real off-pattern detection (an unusual category / amount / recipient / time bumping an invocation to APPROVAL_REQUIRED on top of the static declared tier). Named in Recap §4 and structurally supported by the classifier `Protocol` (a future `OffPatternActionClassifier` can be composed with the static one without touching the broker), but the detector itself needs the four-kinds memory architecture to be queryable, which is still a stub per DRIFTS.md `D-context-assembler-thin-2026-05-09`. Soft-dep; not re-opened here.
  - The customer-facing conversational confirmation UX. The broker returns a structured pending frame; rendering that as a chat-side approval prompt and accepting the customer's natural-language reply ("yes, send it") as approval is the Runtime layer's job and is scoped with Step 31's richer widget UX. The enforcement boundary is closed at the broker today; the conversational shape lands at Step 31.
  - The structured per-invocation audit row write keyed to the same `session_id` / `trace_id`. The broker emits `logger.info` lines with tier+reason+classifier for the interim operator signal; the database audit row is part of the broader widget-chat application-level audit work tracked in `D-widget-chat-no-application-level-audit-log-2026-05-10`. The tier metadata on `ToolResult.metadata` is the contract that downstream audit work will read.
  - Per-tenant tier overrides (e.g. a high-trust tenant downgrading certain notify-and-proceed tools to routine). Out of scope at v1; left to a future Step when there is a paying customer who needs it.
  - LLM-side instruction about the tiered contract. The gate is enforced server-side at the broker; the model does not need to know which tier a tool sits at to call it. A contract that the model has to remember is a contract that degrades silently when the model is swapped. Same rationale as the out-of-band moderation gate in ARCHITECTURE §4.9.
**Prod observed-clean:** Rolled to production on 2026-05-11. ECR image digest `sha256:f0bf303272fb0801eefc4cf0d20d2ddb624f2a5f60c8e845cbe422869739f863` built from `main` HEAD `84339a3` (closing tag target `99c6eb5`) and pushed under ECR tag `step-30c-84339a3`. New task-definition revisions registered against the cluster `luciel-cluster`: `luciel-backend:39` (succeeding rev 38; manifest renamed in repo from `td-backend-rev34.json` to `td-backend-rev39.json` in the same commit as this stanza) and `luciel-worker:19` (succeeding rev 18; manifest renamed from `td-worker-rev14.json` to `td-worker-rev19.json`). Both services accepted the new revisions and rolled forward without invoking the deploymentCircuitBreaker: `luciel-backend-service` showed `PRIMARY :39 running=1 desired=1 failed=0` immediately after the rollover with the old `:38` deployment moving to `DRAINING running=0` on the ALB connection-draining schedule; `luciel-worker-service` showed `PRIMARY :19 running=1 desired=1 failed=0` with the old `:18` deployment going `ACTIVE running=0` immediately. Backend `/ecs/luciel-backend` log group printed the canonical clean-startup sequence (`Started server process [1]` → `Waiting for application startup.` → `Application startup complete.` → `Uvicorn running on http://0.0.0.0:8000`) followed by a steady `GET /health → 200 OK` cadence from both ALB IPs (10.0.10.47 and 10.0.11.10) and zero `ERROR` / `Traceback` / `CRITICAL` hits in the filter window. The runbook used for this rollout is `docs/runbooks/step-30c-action-classification-deploy.md` (committed as `401406d` ahead of the deploy and unchanged during execution). No new environment variables were required: the two new `Settings` knobs (`action_classifier='static'`, `action_classifier_fail_closed=True`) ship with production-correct defaults in `app/core/config.py`, so neither task-def revision needed any `environment` or `secrets` entries beyond the digest update. Real customer-facing traffic on the new revisions began with the first post-rollover `/health 200` returns; the next observable signal as actual tool invocations flow through the gate is `tier_reason='declared_tier'` lines on `ToolResult.metadata`-bearing log records in `/ecs/luciel-backend`. ### ~~D-step-24-5c-impl-backlog-2026-05-11~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-11 (v1 implementation complete on `step-24-5c-*` sub-branches, all five merged to `main`, closing tag cut on the doc-truthing commit). The Step 24.5c roadmap row in CANONICAL_RECAP §12 flipped `📋 Planned` → `✅ Implemented` in this same commit.
**Closing tag:** `step-24-5c-cross-channel-identity-complete`, cut on this doc-truthing commit per the Step 30c `99c6eb5` precedent (so the tag reads "code + docs agree here").
**Implementation arc (as built):** Five sub-branch PRs merged to `main` on 2026-05-11, in order:
  - **PR #24 — sub-branch 1: models + migration.** `app/models/conversation.py` (UUID PK, scope-bearing FKs, `active`, `created_at`, `last_activity_at`); `app/models/identity_claim.py` (UUID PK, native Postgres enum `identity_claim_type` ∈ {EMAIL, PHONE, SSO_SUBJECT}, `user_id` FK to `users.id`, scope-bearing FKs, `issuing_adapter`, nullable `verified_at`, `active`); Alembic migration `3dbbc70d0105` (down_rev `a7c1f4e92b85`) installs both tables plus the load-bearing unique constraint `uq_identity_claims_type_value_scope` on `(claim_type, claim_value, tenant_id, domain_id)` that physically enforces the §4.9 cross-tenant-federation-rejected design. Contract tests: `tests/api/test_step24_5c_models_shape.py` (36 tests).
  - **PR #25 — sub-branch 2: `CrossSessionRetriever`.** `app/memory/cross_session_retriever.py` lands as a sibling of the per-session retriever. Signature: `CrossSessionRetriever(db).retrieve(*, conversation_id, tenant_id, domain_id, limit=20, exclude_session_id=None) -> list[CrossSessionPassage]`. `CrossSessionPassage` is a frozen dataclass with `content`, `role`, `source_session_id`, `source_channel`, `timestamp`, `message_id`. Four-layer scope discipline: input-validation fail-loud at the boundary (TypeError on non-UUID `conversation_id`, ValueError on blank `tenant_id`/`domain_id`), SQL WHERE clause, post-query defense-in-depth loop that re-asserts scope on each materialised row (logs an ERROR and drops the row if it ever fires — operationally impossible via the WHERE, but the defense is the four-layer §4.7 promise made concrete). Contract tests: `tests/api/test_step24_5c_cross_session_retriever_shape.py` (28 tests).
  - **PR #26 — sub-branch 3: `IdentityResolver`.** `app/identity/resolver.py` is the §3.3 step 4 hook. `normalise_claim_value(claim_type, raw)` canonicalises (EMAIL lowercase, PHONE E.164 shape, SSO_SUBJECT opaque); `IdentityResolution` frozen dataclass; `IdentityResolver(db).resolve(*, claim_type, claim_value, tenant_id, domain_id, issuing_adapter) -> IdentityResolution`. Existing-claim path looks up by the unique constraint and returns the bound `User` + most-recent-active `Conversation` under the scope; miss path mints `User` + `IdentityClaim` + `Conversation` in the same SQLAlchemy session (resolver itself does NOT commit — caller owns the transaction, AST-verified). Contract tests: `tests/api/test_step24_5c_identity_resolver_shape.py` (34 tests).
  - **PR #27 — sub-branch 4: adapter claims wiring.** `SessionRepository.create_session()` + `SessionService.create_session()` now accept optional `conversation_id` (legacy path stays untouched if the caller doesn't pass it). New `SessionService.create_session_with_identity(*, tenant_id, domain_id, agent_id, channel, claim_type, claim_value, issuing_adapter) -> SessionWithIdentity` is the ingress-adapter-facing surface that lazy-imports the resolver, runs it inside the same db handle, and creates a session bound to the resolution in one transaction. `SessionWithIdentity` frozen dataclass bundles the new session, the resolved `user_id` / `conversation_id` / `identity_claim_id`, and `is_new_user` / `is_new_conversation` booleans so callers can render the right onboarding UX. Widget + API routes are deliberately NOT touched in this sub-branch — that's deferred to Step 31's richer widget UX work. Contract tests: `tests/api/test_step24_5c_adapter_claims_shape.py` (14 tests).
  - **PR #28 — sub-branch 5: live e2e + this doc-truthing commit.** `tests/e2e/step_24_5c_live_e2e.py` is the partner-level live end-to-end harness (Step 30c precedent shape: runnable script, NOT pytest, exits 0 on all-claims-pass, exits 1 on any-claim-fail, exits 2 on env-not-set-up). Six claim groups exercise the v1 success criterion against the live shipped code: (1) widget adapter mints fresh identity via the §3.3 step 4 hook; (2) widget turn lands and `CrossSessionRetriever` surfaces it both with and without `exclude_session_id`; (3) programmatic API asserts the SAME email and joins the same `user_id` / `conversation_id` / `identity_claim_id`; (4) database state truthing — exactly ONE `identity_claims` row, ONE `conversations` row, TWO sessions, all joined by the same `conversation_id`; (5) programmatic API picks up the widget conversation via the retriever (the headline criterion), with a noise conversation under a different `domain_id` proving the scope filter is honoured; (6) same email under a different `domain_id` mints a separate `User` (the §4.9 cross-tenant-federation rejection enforced at the schema layer). POSTGRES REQUIRED — the harness refuses sqlite at the top because the schema uses a native Postgres enum and UUID columns. Backend-free harness-shape pin in `tests/api/test_step24_5c_live_e2e_shape.py` (10 AST + filesystem invariants — script existence, module-docstring required markers, all four runtime-surface imports, ClaimType + model imports, the non-Postgres refusal guard, the dual exit-code contract, both channel labels named in the success criterion, the `create_session_with_identity` call by name, the `exclude_session_id` kwarg). The shape test runs in the existing backend-free CI job so accidental deletion or signature drift fails CI loudly without needing a live DB.
**Doc-truthing landed in the same commit:** `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §11 Q8 status flipped `📋 Planned (Step 24.5c)` → `✅ Implemented (Step 24.5c, 2026-05-11)` with the closeout stanza naming the three primitives, the §3.3 step 4 hook, and the live e2e proof; §12 Step 24.5c row flipped `📋 Planned` → `✅ Implemented` with the full five-PR closeout, the closing-tag commitment, and pointers to both the live e2e and the shape pin. `ARCHITECTURE.md` §3.2.11 lead-in flipped `📋 Design committed` → `✅ Implemented` with the five-PR breakdown and the live-e2e + shape-pin pointers; §3.3 step 5 cross-session-retriever marker flipped `📋` → `✅`; both §4.9 rejected-alternative bullets flipped `📋` → `✅` (the cross-tenant-federation bullet now names the unique-constraint mechanism that physically enforces the rejection, plus the live e2e CLAIM 6 that proves it).
**Deliberate non-goals at v1, carried forward as not-regressions:** (same list the open block carried) end-user-driven claim verification (Step 34a + Step 31); cross-tenant identity federation (Step 38 — physically rejected at the schema layer in v1); a per-`User` inbox view spanning all channels (Step 31 dashboards); the voice / SMS / email channel adapters themselves (Step 34a — the §3.2.11 primitives are framework-ready for them). Widget + programmatic-API ROUTE wiring (the request-time path that calls `create_session_with_identity` instead of `create_session`) is also deferred to Step 31's richer widget UX work; the §3.3 step 4 service surface is built and proven end-to-end against real Postgres, but the routes still take the legacy `create_session` path until Step 31 lands the embed-key→User claim assertion alongside its onboarding UX.
**Test totals:** 112 contract tests across sub-branches 1–4 (36 + 28 + 34 + 14) plus the 10-test harness-shape pin in sub-branch 5 = 122 backend-free tests pinning the Step 24.5c surface. The live e2e (six claim groups, ~30 individual claims) runs against a developer's Postgres dev DB on demand and on the doc-truthing commit — it is the integration proof that the four sub-branches compose into the v1 success criterion.
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.11 (now ✅, names this drift in past tense); ARCHITECTURE §3.3 step 5 (now ✅); ARCHITECTURE §4.9 (both bullets now ✅; the cross-tenant-federation bullet names the unique-constraint mechanism); CANONICAL_RECAP §11 Q8 (now ✅); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 24.5c row (now ✅; names the five PRs and both proofs); `tests/e2e/step_24_5c_live_e2e.py` (the v1 live-e2e proof, Postgres-only); `tests/e2e/README.md` (per-step live-e2e harness precedent — Step 24.5c is the second step on the project to ship one, after Step 30c); `tests/api/test_step24_5c_live_e2e_shape.py` (backend-free harness-shape pin); `tests/api/test_step24_5c_{models,cross_session_retriever,identity_resolver,adapter_claims}_shape.py` (sub-branch 1–4 contract tests); `D-channels-only-chat-implemented-2026-05-09` (Step 34a — the 24.5c primitives are framework-ready for voice/SMS/email when those adapters land); `D-context-assembler-thin-2026-05-09` (adjacent — cross-session retriever output will join per-session memory at context-assembly time when that consolidation work happens; not a 24.5c gating dep). ### ~~D-widget-chat-no-application-level-audit-log-2026-05-10~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-12 (Step 31 sub-branch 1 merged to `main`).
**Closing commit:** `5723b8e` (Step 31 sub-branch 1: widget chat audit log + `create_session_with_identity` wiring, PR #30).
**Resolution:** `app/api/v1/chat_widget.py` now emits three structured `logger.info` lines per widget turn — `widget_chat_turn_received` at request entry (`tenant_id`, `domain_id`, `embed_key_prefix`, `agent_id`, `luciel_instance_id`, message length), `widget_chat_session_resolved` after lazy session creation (`session_id`, `user_id`, `conversation_id`, `is_new_user`, `is_new_conversation`), and `widget_chat_turn_completed` after the stream finishes (`session_id`, `latency_ms`, `model`, `provider`, `tokens_emitted`, `blocked_by_moderation`). The lazy-session path was simultaneously swapped from `session_service.create_session(...user_id=None...)` to `session_service.create_session_with_identity(...)` when the embed-key request carries a `client_claim`, falling back to the anonymous path when it does not. Backend-free contract test `tests/api/test_step31_chat_audit_shape.py` pins all three emission sites by AST search, asserts each carries the documented field set, asserts `create_session_with_identity` is reachable from the widget route when `client_claim` is present, and asserts no `logger.info` from this module ever carries a raw message body (PII defense). The §3.3 step 4 identity-resolver hook from Step 24.5c is therefore now route-wired for the widget surface — the carried-forward route-wiring item from Step 24.5c PR #27 also closes here for the widget channel (programmatic-API route wiring remains carried forward to a future step).
**Cross-refs:** ARCHITECTURE §3.2.7 (Application log stream — widget bullet now ✅); CANONICAL_RECAP §12 Step 31 row (now ✅, the validation-gate harness exercises this structured-log path under the CUSTOMER_JOURNEY pillar); `tests/api/test_step31_chat_audit_shape.py` (backend-free shape pin); `tests/e2e/step_31_validation_gate.py` (live-Postgres harness that exercises the widget→audit-log→trace→dashboard chain end-to-end).

Each method treats the caller's resolved scope as the **upper bound** of what it can read, never as a hint. All aggregates query existing `traces` + scope tables (no new DB writes). Embed-key denial pinned at the perimeter (none of the three endpoints reachable from a `key_kind='embed'` credential). Backend-free contract test pins endpoint registration + embed-key denial. Merged as `ec6af5c`.
  - **PR #33 — sub-branch 4: five-pillar validation-gate harness.** `tests/e2e/step_31_validation_gate.py` is the Postgres-required, runnable-script live e2e in the Step 30c / Step 24.5c precedent (POSTGRES REQUIRED, exits 0 on all-green, 1 on any-fail, 2 on env-not-set-up, idempotent timestamp-suffixed fixture tenants `step31_gate_A_<stamp>` / `_B_<stamp>` so re-runs never collide). Five claim groups, one per pillar: (i) **ISOLATION** — two-tenant seeding with overlapping shapes, every dashboard call from one cannot see the other's data; (ii) **CUSTOMER_JOURNEY** — widget channel turn through `create_session_with_identity` → audit row emitted → trace row written → dashboard reflects the turn; (iii) **MEMORY_QUALITY** — programmatic_api second turn re-uses conversation, cross-tenant denied; (iv) **OPERATIONS** — seven named alarms present in `cfn/luciel-prod-alarms.yaml` (WorkerNoHeartbeatAlarm, WorkerUnhealthyTaskCountAlarm, WorkerErrorLogRateAlarm, RdsConnectionCountAlarm, RdsCpuAlarm, RdsFreeStorageAlarm, SsmAccessFailureAlarm); (v) **COMPLIANCE** — `admin_audit_logs` hash chain intact across the seeded run, `deletion_logs` shape present. Backend-free harness-shape pin in `tests/api/test_step31_validation_gate_shape.py`. Merged as `6b85bf1`.
  - **PR #34 — sub-branch 5: live e2e + this doc-truthing commit.** The harness was driven against live Postgres on 2026-05-12 (run stamp `20260512-144847-068362`), exited 0 with 40/40 claims green across all five pillars (isolation 8/8, customer_journey 11/11, memory_quality 6/6, operations 9/9, compliance 6/6), and this doc-truthing commit re-cuts the closing tag forward onto the merge where code and all three docs first agree. One PR #33 outlier surfaced and was corrected in the same commit: harness line 100 imported `SessionLocal` from a fictional `app.db.database` module (canonical path is `app.db.session`, used by every other importer in the codebase — middleware, worker, verification pillars, scripts), proving PR #33's harness was merged without ever being executed end-to-end; surfaced honestly here rather than silently fixed, per §6/§7 doctrine. Driver-suffix observation worth recording: the harness module docstring suggests `postgresql+psycopg2://...` but the stack uses psycopg v3 (`postgresql+psycopg://...`) and the import-time guard accepts both — no fix needed, but the docstring is a future hygiene candidate.
**Doc-truthing landed in the same commit:** `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §12 Step 31 row flipped `📋 Planned` → `✅ Implemented` with the five-PR closeout, the closing-tag commitment, the named pillars + alarm list, and pointers to both the harness and the shape pin. `ARCHITECTURE.md` §3.2.7 (Application log stream — widget bullet) flipped `📋` → `✅`; §3.2.12 (Hierarchical dashboards & validation gate) markers flipped `📋` → `✅ Implemented` with the live-harness + shape-pin pointers.

### ~~D-doc-truthing-pass-3-overstep-and-recap-last-updated-sediment-2026-05-13~~

**Status:** RESOLVED on 2026-05-13 by PR #41 (`step-31-doc-truthing-pass-4-remove-sediment-and-doctrine-section`, merged as `40b2acf`). Entry retained in §3 unchanged per §6 (move-to-§5 with strikethrough, do **not** delete from §3).
**Closing commit:** `361eaad` (PR #41), merged to `main` as `40b2acf`.
**Resolution:** PR #41 removed the "Last updated" sediment paragraph from `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` line 9 entirely, and removed the §18 (recap) / §8 (architecture) / §8 (drifts) parallel "Triangulation discipline" sections that PR #40 had introduced. Net change − 69 lines across the three docs, returning each to its pre-PR-#40 section structure (recap ends at §17, architecture ends at §7, drifts at §7). The cross-document clarification survives as one folded line inside `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` §17 and `ARCHITECTURE.md` §6, pointing at `DRIFTS.md` §1 + §6 as the canonical home of the doctrine — the same home the doctrine was already in before PR #40 invented parallel sections.
**Doctrine reflection (recorded for future passes):** Both breaches happened within the doc-truthing arc that was supposed to be tightening the audit story. The lesson is not that doctrine is hard — it's that the temptation to *demonstrate* doctrine through new top-level sections, or to mark a pass's progress at the top of a doc, is exactly the failure mode each doc's maintenance section already forbids. The doctrine demonstrates itself by being followed silently in the commit log, the section markers, and the §3/§5 lifecycle — not by being announced as a new section. This pass 5 closure is itself the demonstration: an honest §3/§5 record of two breaches and their fix, no new sections, no top-of-file sediment.
**Cross-refs:** PR #36 (`d843812`), PR #38 (`f359d5f`), PR #39 (`c5aec38`) — grew the "Last updated" paragraph; PR #40 (`09c6ddd`) — introduced §18 / §8 / §8 over-step; PR #41 (`40b2acf`) — corrected both; CANONICAL_RECAP §17; ARCHITECTURE §6; DRIFTS §1 line 30 + §6 line 495 (canonical home of cross-document source-of-truth doctrine, unchanged throughout the arc).

### Step 29.z — Repo-vs-Design audit (no findings)

**Status:** AUDIT COMPLETE on 2026-05-09; no fix-here drifts surfaced.
**Audit scope:** Treat `CANONICAL_RECAP.md`, `ARCHITECTURE.md`, and `DRIFTS.md` as ground truth; walk the repo top-down; for any divergence, classify as fix-here, new drift, or doc edit. Sandbox-only, no behavior changes, no AWS, no production touched.
**What was checked:** repo top-level layout; `app/` mapped to the six-component model (Persona, Runtime, Memory, Tool, Policy, Observability) plus the four cross-cutting concerns (scope isolation, audit chain, Pattern E, retention); 25 verification pillars file presence; alembic migration count and recency; tenant-vs-scope terminology footprint (113 files, ~2000 occurrences); root-level task-definition manifests; runtime stub depth.
**Result:** Zero material code-vs-doc misalignments that warrant a repo fix in this branch. Every gap that surfaced during the audit was already an open drift in Section 3 (`D-context-assembler-thin`, `D-celery-task-surface-thin`, `D-retention-purge-worker-missing`, `D-confirmation-gate-not-enforced`, `D-channels-only-chat-implemented`, `D-external-integrations-llm-only`) and is owned by an existing roadmap step (30c, 34, 34a). Cosmetic items deliberately not pursued: pillar filename `cross_tenant_*` vs doc concept `scope_leak` (renaming would touch the verification entry points without changing behavior); root-level `td-*.json` task-def manifests (intentionally tracked, referenced by deployment runbooks). The `tenant` term is preserved throughout the codebase as the legitimate top-of-hierarchy scope-level name per the resolution of `D-tenant-language-vs-scope-language-2026-05-09`.
**Why this entry exists:** A no-findings audit is itself a finding worth recording — it certifies that on this date, with these three docs as ground truth, the repo was aligned. Future drift hunts can anchor against this baseline. The `step-29z-repo-reconciliation` branch was cut and abandoned without commits because there was nothing to ship.
**Closing commit:** this commit.

---

## Section 6 — How drifts are added, closed, or reopened

**Adding a drift.** Append to Section 3 (open) or Section 4 (production-pending), with a fresh `D-<slug>-YYYY-MM-DD` id, a status, the section that raised it, the design claim, the repo or prod state, and a resolution path. Do not add to closed-drift section while the drift is still open.

**Closing a drift.** Move the entry verbatim to Section 5, wrap the heading in `~~strikethrough~~`, fill in the closing commit (and tag if relevant) and a one-line resolution. Do not delete the entry from Section 3 — move it. The audit chain depends on the body of each drift remaining readable after closure.

**Reopening a drift.** Open a new drift with a fresh id and a date suffix matching the day of reopening. Reference the closed predecessor in the body. The closed predecessor stays closed; reopening is a new story.

**Marker propagation.** As drifts close, the corresponding section in `ARCHITECTURE.md` or `CANONICAL_RECAP.md` gets the appropriate ✅ / 🔧 / 📋 / 🔬 marker added in surgical edits. The marker is the connective tissue between the design docs and this register; the doc edit and the drift closure are part of the same commit.

**What does NOT belong in the design docs.** The three canonical docs (`CANONICAL_RECAP.md`, `ARCHITECTURE.md`, `DRIFTS.md`) are stable references, not running notebooks. Build-time detail — framework choice, library selection, schema column lists, transport-protocol rationale, branding-knob inventories, sandbox demo plans — belongs in **commit messages** and **code-level docstrings**, not in the canonical docs. The canonical docs grow only when the architectural shape changes: a new cross-cutting property, a new component, a deletion of something that is no longer true, or a roadmap step landing such that its success criterion is provably met. A new roadmap step, on its own, is not a reason to grow the docs — the recap row already exists, and implementation detail is recoverable from `git log` and the code itself. If a build genuinely needs a multi-day shared scratchpad, it lives in `docs/in-flight/<slug>.md` during the build and is **deleted** (not archived) on merge. This principle exists because docs that grow with every roadmap step become unparsable; the discipline of keeping them stable is what makes them useful as references.

---

## Section 7 — Source-of-truth rule

If a chat summary, a session recap, a slide, an email, or any other artifact contradicts this document about the status of a drift, **this document wins**. Update the document; do not let the contradicting artifact stand.
